10095-8{_}662{_}And by this was a great pile of the heads of men, and warriors were continually casting more and more upon the heap.
10095-8{_}663{_}"'How many?'
10095-8{_}664{_}asked Abdallah.
10095-8{_}665{_}"'Twelve thousand, O Apostle of God,' answered they, 'but there are more to come.'
10095-8{_}666{_}"'Thou monster!'
10095-8{_}667{_}said I to Abdallah.
10095-8{_}668{_}"'Nay, father,' said he, 'there will not be more than sixteen thousand in all, and these men were unbelievers.
10095-8{_}669{_}Moreover we have spared such of their women as were young and handsome, and have taken them for our concubines, as is ordained in the eleventh supplement to the Book of Ad, just promulgated by my authority.
10095-8{_}670{_}But come, I have other things to manifest unto thee.'
10095-8{_}671{_}"And he led me where a stake was driven into the earth, and a man was chained unto it, and fuel was heaped all around him, and many stood by with lighted torches in their hands.
10095-8{_}672{_}"'O Abdallah,' I exclaimed, 'wherefore this atrocity?'
10095-8{_}673{_}"'This man,' he replied, 'is a blasphemer, who hath said that the Book of Ad is written on the bones of a cow.'
10095-8{_}674{_}"'But it is written on the bones of a cow!
10095-8{_}675{_}'I cried.
10095-8{_}676{_}"'Even so,' said he, 'and therefore is his heresy the more damnable, and his punishment the more exemplary.
10095-8{_}677{_}Had it been indeed written on the bones of a camel, he might have affirmed what pleased him.'
10095-8{_}678{_}"And I shook off the dust from my feet, and hastened to my dwelling.
10095-8{_}679{_}The rest of Abdallah's acts thou knowest, and how he fell warring with the Carmathians.
10095-8{_}680{_}And now I ask thee, art thou yet minded to go forth as a missionary of the truth?"
10095-8{_}681{_}"O Sergius," said the young man, "I perceive that the temptations are greater, and the difficulties far surpassing what I had thought.
10095-8{_}682{_}Yet will I go, and I trust by Heaven's grace not to fail utterly."
10095-8{_}683{_}"Then go," said Sergius, "and Heaven's blessing go with thee!
10095-8{_}684{_}Come back in ten years, should I be living, and if thou canst declare that thou hast forged no scriptures, and worked no miracles, and persecuted no unbelievers, and flattered no potentate, and bribed no one with the promise of aught in heaven or earth, I will give thee the philosopher's stone."
10095-8{_}685{_}ANANDA THE MIRACLE WORKER   The holy Buddha, Sakhya Muni, on dispatching his apostles to proclaim his religion throughout the peninsula of India, failed not to provide them with salutary precepts for their guidance.
10095-8{_}686{_}He exhorted them to meekness, to compassion, to abstemiousness, to zeal in the promulgation of his doctrine, and added an injunction never before or since prescribed by the founder of any religion--namely, on no account to perform any miracle.
10095-8{_}687{_}It is further related, that whereas the apostles experienced considerable difficulty in complying with the other instructions of their master, and sometimes actually failed therein, the prohibition to work miracles was never once transgressed by any of them, save only the pious Ananda, the history of whose first year's apostolate is recorded as follows.
10095-8{_}688{_}Ananda repaired to the kingdom of Magadha, and instructed the inhabitants diligently in the law of Buddha.
10095-8{_}689{_}His doctrine being acceptable, and his speech persuasive, the people hearkened to him willingly, and began to forsake the Brahmins whom they had previously revered as spiritual guides.
10095-8{_}690{_}Perceiving this, Ananda became elated in spirit, and one day he exclaimed:  "How blessed is the apostle who propagates truth by the efficacy of reason and virtuous example, combined with eloquence, rather than error by imposture and devil-mongering, like those miserable Brahmins!"
10095-8{_}691{_}As he uttered this vainglorious speech, the mountain of his merits was diminished by sixteen yojanas, and virtue and efficacy departed from him, insomuch that when he next addressed the multitude they first mocked, then hooted, and finally pelted him.
10095-8{_}692{_}When matters had reached this pass, Ananda lifted his eyes and discerned a number of Brahmins of the lower sort, busy about a boy who lay in a fit upon the ground.
10095-8{_}693{_}They had long been applying exorcisms and other approved methods with scant success, when the most sagacious among them suggested:  "Let us render the body of this patient an uncomfortable residence for the demon; peradventure he will then cease to abide therein."
10095-8{_}694{_}They were accordingly engaged in branding the sufferer with hot irons, filling his nostrils with smoke, and otherwise to the best of their ability disquieting the intrusive devil.
10095-8{_}695{_}Ananda's first thought was, "The lad is in a fit;" the second, "It were a pious deed to deliver him from his tormentors;" the third, "By good management this may extricate me from my present uncomfortable predicament, and redound to the glory of the most holy Buddha."
10095-8{_}696{_}Yielding to this temptation, he strode forward, chased away the Brahmins with an air of authority, and, uplifting his countenance to heaven, recited the appellations of seven devils.
10095-8{_}697{_}No effect ensuing,  he repeated seven more, and so continued until, the fit having passed off in the course of nature, the patient's paroxysms ceased, he opened his eyes, and Ananda restored him to his relatives.
10095-8{_}698{_}But the people cried loudly, "A miracle!
10095-8{_}699{_}a miracle!"
10095-8{_}700{_}and when Ananda resumed his instructions, they gave heed to him, and numbers embraced the religion of Buddha.
10095-8{_}701{_}Whereupon Ananda exulted, and applauded himself for his dexterity and presence of mind, and said to himself:  "Surely the end sanctifies the means."
10095-8{_}702{_}As he propounded this heresy, the eminence of his merits was reduced to the dimensions of a mole-hill, and he ceased to be of account in the eyes of any of the saints, save only of Buddha, whose compassion is inexhaustible.
10095-8{_}703{_}The fame of his achievement, nevertheless, was bruited about the whole country, and soon reached the ears of the king, who sent for him, and inquired if he had actually expelled the demon.
10095-8{_}704{_}Ananda replied in the affirmative.
10095-8{_}705{_}"I am indeed rejoiced," returned the king, "as thou now wilt without doubt proceed to heal _my_ son, who has lain in a trance for twenty-nine days."
10095-8{_}706{_}"Alas!
10095-8{_}707{_}dread sovereign," modestly returned Ananda, "how should the merits which barely suffice to effect the cure of a miserable Pariah avail to restore the offspring of an Elephant among Kings?"
10095-8{_}708{_}"By what process are these merits acquired?"
10095-8{_}709{_}demanded the monarch.
10095-8{_}710{_}"By the exercise of penance," responded Ananda, "in virtue of which the austere devotee  quells the winds, allays the waters, expostulates convincingly with tigers, carries the moon in his sleeve, and otherwise performs all acts and deeds appropriate to the character of a peripatetic thaumaturgist."
10095-8{_}711{_}"This being so," answered the king, "thy inability to heal my son manifestly arises from defect of merit, and defect of merit from defect of penance.
10095-8{_}712{_}I will therefore consign thee to the charge of my Brahmins, that they may aid thee to fill up the measure of that which is lacking."
10095-8{_}713{_}Ananda vainly strove to explain that the austerities to which he had referred were entirely of a spiritual and contemplative character.
10095-8{_}714{_}The Brahmins, enchanted to get a heretic into their clutches, immediately seized upon him, and conveyed him to one of their temples.
10095-8{_}715{_}They stripped him, and perceived with astonishment that not one single weal or scar was visible anywhere on his person.
10095-8{_}716{_}"Horror!"
10095-8{_}717{_}they exclaimed; "here is a man who expects to go to heaven in a whole skin!"
10095-8{_}718{_}To obviate this breach of etiquette, they laid him upon his face, and flagellated him until the obnoxious soundness of cuticle was entirely removed.
10095-8{_}719{_}They then departed, promising to return next day and operate in a corresponding manner upon the anterior part of his person, after which, they jeeringly assured him, his merits would be in no respect less than those of the saintly Bhagiratha, or of the regal Viswamitra himself.
10095-8{_}720{_}Ananda lay half dead upon the floor of the temple, when the sanctuary was illuminated by the apparition of a resplendent Glendoveer, who thus addressed him:  "Well, backsliding disciple, art thou yet convinced of thy folly?"
10095-8{_}721{_}Ananda relished neither the imputation on his orthodoxy nor that on his wisdom.
10095-8{_}722{_}He replied, notwithstanding, with all meekness:  "Heaven forbid that I should repine at any variety of martyrdom that tends to the propagation of my master's faith."
10095-8{_}723{_}"Wilt thou then first be healed, and moreover become the instrument of converting the entire realm of Magadha?"
10095-8{_}724{_}"How shall this be accomplished?"
10095-8{_}725{_}demanded Ananda.
10095-8{_}726{_}"By perseverance in the path of deceit and disobedience," returned the Glendoveer.
10095-8{_}727{_}Ananda winced, but maintained silence in the expectation of more explicit directions.
10095-8{_}728{_}"Know," pursued the spirit, "that the king's son will revive from his trance at the expiration of the thirtieth day, which takes place at noon to-morrow.
10095-8{_}729{_}Thou hast but to proceed at the fitting period to the couch whereon he is deposited, and, placing thy hand upon his heart, to command him to rise forthwith.
10095-8{_}730{_}His recovery will be ascribed to thy supernatural powers, and the establishment of Buddha's religion will result.
10095-8{_}731{_}Before this it will be needful that I should perform an actual cure upon thy back, which is within the compass of my capacity.
10095-8{_}732{_}I only request thee to take notice, that thou wilt on this occasion be transgressing the precepts of thy master with thine eyes open.
10095-8{_}733{_}It is also meet to apprise thee that thy temporary extrication from thy present difficulties will only involve thee in others still more formidable."
10095-8{_}734{_}"An incorporeal Glendoveer is no judge of the feelings of a flayed apostle," thought Ananda.
10095-8{_}735{_}"Heal me," he replied, "if thou canst, and reserve thy admonitions for a more convenient opportunity."
10095-8{_}736{_}"So be it," returned the Glendoveer; and as he extended his hand over Ananda, the latter's back was clothed anew with skin, and his previous smart simultaneously allayed.
10095-8{_}737{_}The Glendoveer vanished at the same moment, saying, "When thou hast need of me, pronounce but the incantation, _Gnooh Imdap Inam Mua_, [*] and I will immediately be by thy side."
10095-8{_}738{_}[Footnote: The mystic formula of the Buddhists, read backwards.]
10095-8{_}739{_}The anger and amazement of the Brahmins may be conceived when, on returning equipped with fresh implements of flagellation, they discovered the salubrious condition of their victim.
10095-8{_}740{_}Their scourges would probably have undergone conversion into halters, had they not been accompanied by a royal officer, who took the really triumphant martyr under his protection, and carried him off to the palace.
10095-8{_}741{_}He was speedily conducted to the young prince's couch, whither a vast crowd attended him.
10095-8{_}742{_}The hour of noon not having yet arrived, Ananda discreetly protracted the time by a seasonable discourse on the impossibility of miracles, those only excepted which should be wrought by the professors of the faith of Buddha.
10095-8{_}743{_}He then descended from his pulpit, and precisely as the sun attained the zenith laid his hand upon the bosom of the young prince, who instantly revived, and completed a sentence touching the game of dice which had been interrupted by his catalepsy.
10095-8{_}744{_}The people shouted, the courtiers went into ecstasies, the countenances of the Brahmins assumed an exceedingly sheepish expression.
10095-8{_}745{_}Even the king seemed impressed, and craved to be more particularly instructed in the law of Buddha.
10095-8{_}746{_}In complying with this request, Ananda, who had made marvellous progress in worldly wisdom during the last twenty-four hours, deemed it needless to dilate on the cardinal doctrines of his master, the misery of existence, the need of redemption, the path to felicity, the prohibition to shed blood.
10095-8{_}747{_}He simply stated that the priests of Buddha were bound to perpetual poverty, and that under the new dispensation all ecclesiastical property would accrue to the temporal authorities.
10095-8{_}748{_}"By the holy cow!"
10095-8{_}749{_}exclaimed the monarch, "this is something like a religion!"
10095-8{_}750{_}The words were scarcely out of the royal lips ere the courtiers professed themselves converts.
10095-8{_}751{_}The multitude followed their example.
10095-8{_}752{_}The Brahminical church was promptly disestablished and disendowed, and more injustice was committed in the name of the new and purified religion in one day than the old corrupt one had occasioned in a hundred years.
10095-8{_}753{_}Ananda had the satisfaction of feeling able to forgive his adversaries, and of valuing himself accordingly; and to complete his felicity, he was received in the palace, and entrusted with the education of the king's son, which he strove to conduct agreeably to the precepts of Buddha.
10095-8{_}754{_}This was a task of some delicacy, as it involved interference with the princely youth's favourite amusement, which had previously consisted in torturing small reptiles.
10095-8{_}755{_}After a short interval Ananda was again summoned to the monarch's presence.
10095-8{_}756{_}He found his majesty in the company of two most ferocious ruffians, one of whom bore a huge axe, and the other an enormous pair of pincers.
10095-8{_}757{_}"My chief executioner and my chief tormentor," said the king.
10095-8{_}758{_}Ananda expressed his gratification at becoming acquainted with such exalted functionaries.
10095-8{_}759{_}"Thou must know, most holy man," resumed the king, "that need has again arisen for the exercise of fortitude and self-denial on thy part.
10095-8{_}760{_}A powerful enemy has invaded my dominions, and has impiously presumed to discomfit my troops.
10095-8{_}761{_}Well might I feel dismayed, were it not for the consolations of religion; but my trust is in thee, O spiritual father!
10095-8{_}762{_}It is urgent that thou shouldst accumulate the largest amount of merit with the least delay possible.
10095-8{_}763{_}I am unable to invoke the ministrations of thy old friends the Brahmins to this end, they being, as thou knowest, in disgrace, but I have summoned these trusty and experienced counsellors in their room.
10095-8{_}764{_}I find them not wholly in accord.
10095-8{_}765{_}My chief tormentor, being a man of mild temper and humane disposition, considers that it might at first suffice to employ gentle measures, such, for example, as suspending thee head downwards in the smoke of a wood fire, and filling thy nostrils with red pepper.
10095-8{_}766{_}My chief executioner, taking, peradventure, a too professional view of the subject, deems it best to resort at once to crucifixion or impalement.
10095-8{_}767{_}I would gladly know thy thoughts on the matter."
10095-8{_}768{_}Ananda expressed, as well as his terror would  suffer him, his entire disapproval of both the courses recommended by the royal advisers.
10095-8{_}769{_}"Well," said the king, with an air of resignation, "if we cannot agree upon either, it follows that we must try both.
10095-8{_}770{_}We will meet for that purpose to-morrow morning at the second hour.
10095-8{_}771{_}Go in peace!"
10095-8{_}772{_}Ananda went, but not in peace.
10095-8{_}773{_}His alarm would have well-nigh deprived him of his faculties if he had not remembered the promise made him by his former deliverer.
10095-8{_}774{_}On reaching a secluded spot he pronounced the mystic formula, and immediately became aware of the presence, not of a radiant Glendoveer, but of a holy man, whose head was strewn with ashes, and his body anointed with cow-dung.
10095-8{_}775{_}"Thy occasion," said the Fakir, "brooks no delay.
10095-8{_}776{_}Thou must immediately accompany me, and assume the garb of a Jogi."
10095-8{_}777{_}Ananda rebelled excessively in his heart, for he had imbibed from the mild and sage Buddha a befitting contempt for these grotesque and cadaverous fanatics.
10095-8{_}778{_}The emergency, however, left him no resource, and he followed his guide to a charnel house, which the latter had selected as his domicile.
10095-8{_}779{_}There, with many lamentations over the smoothness of his hair and the brevity of his nails, the Jogi besprinkled and besmeared Ananda agreeably to his own pattern, and scored him with chalk and ochre until the peaceful apostle of the gentlest of creeds resembled a Bengal tiger.
10095-8{_}780{_}He then hung a chaplet of infants' skulls about his neck, placed the skull of a malefactor in one of his hands and the thigh-bone of a necromancer in the other, and at nightfall conducted him into the  adjacent cemetery, where, seating him on the ashes of a recent funeral pile, he bade him drum upon the skull with the thigh-bone, and repeat after himself the incantations which he began to scream out towards the western part of the firmament.
10095-8{_}781{_}These charms were apparently possessed of singular efficacy, for scarcely were they commenced ere a hideous tempest arose, rain descended in torrents, phosphoric flashes darted across the sky, wolves and hyænas thronged howling from their dens, and gigantic goblins, arising from the earth, extended their fleshless arms towards Ananda, and strove to drag him from his seat.
10095-8{_}782{_}Urged by frantic terror, and the example and exhortations of his companion, he battered, banged, and vociferated, until on the very verge of exhaustion; when, as if by enchantment, the tempest ceased, the spectres disappeared, and joyous shouts and a burst of music announced the occurrence of something auspicious in the adjoining city.
10095-8{_}783{_}"The hostile king is dead," said the Jogi; "and his army has dispersed.
10095-8{_}784{_}This will be attributed to thy incantations.
10095-8{_}785{_}They are coming in quest of thee even now.
10095-8{_}786{_}Farewell until thou again hast need of me."
10095-8{_}787{_}The Jogi disappeared, the tramp of a procession became audible, and soon torches glared feebly through the damp, cheerless dawn.
10095-8{_}788{_}The monarch descended from his state elephant, and, prostrating himself before Ananda, exclaimed:  "Inestimable man!
10095-8{_}789{_}why didst thou not disclose that thou wert a Jogi?
10095-8{_}790{_}Never more shall I feel the least apprehension of any of my enemies, so long as thou continuest an inmate of this cemetery."
10095-8{_}791{_}A family of jackals were unceremoniously dislodged from a disused sepulchre, which was allotted to Ananda for his future residence.
10095-8{_}792{_}The king permitted no alteration in his costume, and took care that the food doled out to him should have no tendency to impair his sanctity, which speedily gave promise of attaining a very high pitch.
10095-8{_}793{_}His hair had already become as matted and his nails as long as the Jogi could have desired, when he received a visit from another royal messenger.
10095-8{_}794{_}The Rajah, so ran the regal missive, had been suddenly and mysteriously attacked by a dangerous malady, but confidently anticipated relief from Ananda's merits and incantations.
10095-8{_}795{_}Ananda resumed his thigh-bone and his skull, and ruefully began to thump the latter with the former, in dismal expectation of the things that were to come.
10095-8{_}796{_}But the spell seemed to have lost its potency.
10095-8{_}797{_}Nothing more unearthly than a bat presented itself, and Ananda was beginning to think that he might as well desist when his reflections were diverted by the apparition of a tall and grave personage, wearing a sad-coloured robe, and carrying a long wand, who stood by his side as suddenly as though just risen from the earth.
10095-8{_}798{_}"The caldron is ready," said the stranger.
10095-8{_}799{_}"What caldron?"
10095-8{_}800{_}demanded Ananda.
10095-8{_}801{_}"That wherein thou art about to be immersed."
10095-8{_}802{_}"I immersed in a caldron!
10095-8{_}803{_}wherefore?"
10095-8{_}804{_}"Thy spells," returned his interlocutor, "having hitherto failed to afford his majesty the slightest relief, and his experience of their efficacy on a former occasion forbidding him to suppose that they can be inoperative, he is naturally led to ascribe to their pernicious influence that aggravation of pain of which he has for some time past unfortunately been sensible.
10095-8{_}805{_}I have confirmed him in this conjecture, esteeming it for the interest of science that his anger should fall upon an impudent impostor like thee rather than on a discreet and learned physician like myself.
10095-8{_}806{_}He has consequently directed the principal caldron to be kept boiling all night, intending to immerse thee therein at daybreak, unless he should in the meantime derive some benefit from thy conjurations."
10095-8{_}807{_}"Heavens!"
10095-8{_}808{_}exclaimed Ananda, "whither shall I fly?"
10095-8{_}809{_}"Nowhere beyond this cemetery," returned the physician, "inasmuch as it is entirely surrounded by the royal forces."
10095-8{_}810{_}"Wherein, then," demanded the agonized apostle, "doth the path of safety lie?"
10095-8{_}811{_}"In this phial," answered the physician.
10095-8{_}812{_}"It contains a subtle poison.
10095-8{_}813{_}Demand to be led before the king.
10095-8{_}814{_}Affirm that thou hast received a sovereign medicine from the hands of benignant spirits.
10095-8{_}815{_}He will drink it and perish, and thou wilt be richly rewarded by his successor."
10095-8{_}816{_}"Ayaunt, tempter!"
10095-8{_}817{_}cried Ananda, hurling the phial indignantly away.
10095-8{_}818{_}"I defy thee!
10095-8{_}819{_}and will have recourse to my old deliverer--_Gnooh Imdap Inam Mua!
10095-8{_}820{_}"_  But the charm appeared to fail of its effect.
10095-8{_}821{_}No figure was visible to his gaze, save that of the physician, who seemed to regard him with an expression of pity as he gathered up his robes and melted rather than glided into the encompassing darkness.
10095-8{_}822{_}Ananda remained, contending with himself.
10095-8{_}823{_}Countless times was he on the point of calling  after the physician and imploring him to return with a potion of like properties to the one rejected, but something seemed always to rise in his throat and impede his utterance, until, worn out by agitation, he fell asleep and dreamed this dream.
10095-8{_}824{_}He thought he stood at the vast and gloomy entrance of Patala.
10095-8{_}825{_}[*] The lugubrious spot wore a holiday appearance; everything seemed to denote a diabolical gala.
10095-8{_}826{_}Swarms of demons of all shapes and sizes beset the portal, contemplating what appeared to be preparations for an illumination.
10095-8{_}827{_}Strings of coloured lamps were in course of disposition in wreaths and festoons by legions of frolicsome imps, chattering, laughing, and swinging by their tails like so many monkeys.
10095-8{_}828{_}The operation was directed from below by superior fiends of great apparent gravity and respectability.
10095-8{_}829{_}These bore wands of office, tipped with yellow flames, wherewith they singed the tails of the imps when such discipline appeared to them to be requisite.
10095-8{_}830{_}Ananda could not refrain from asking the reason of these festive preparations.
10095-8{_}831{_}[Footnote: The Hindoo Pandemonium.]
10095-8{_}832{_}"They are in honour," responded the demon interrogated, "of the pious Ananda, one of the apostles of the Lord Buddha, whose advent is hourly expected among us with much eagerness and satisfaction."
10095-8{_}833{_}The horrified Ananda with much difficulty mustered resolution to inquire on what account the apostle in question was necessitated to take up his abode in the infernal regions.
10095-8{_}834{_}"On account of poisoning," returned the fiend laconically.
10095-8{_}835{_}Ananda was about to seek further explanations, when his attention was arrested by a violent altercation between two of the supervising demons.
10095-8{_}836{_}"Kammuragha, evidently," croaked one.
10095-8{_}837{_}"Damburanana, of course," snarled the other.
10095-8{_}838{_}"May I," inquired Ananda of the fiend he had before addressed, "presume to ask the signification of Kammuragha and Damburanana?"
10095-8{_}839{_}"They are two hells," replied the demon.
10095-8{_}840{_}"In Kammuragha the occupant is plunged into melted pitch and fed with melted lead.
10095-8{_}841{_}In Damburanana he is plunged into melted lead and fed with melted pitch.
10095-8{_}842{_}My colleagues are debating which is the more appropriate to the demerits of our guest Ananda."
10095-8{_}843{_}Ere Ananda had had time to digest this announcement a youthful imp descended from above with agility, and, making a profound reverence, presented himself before the disputants.
10095-8{_}844{_}"Venerable demons," interposed he, "might my insignificance venture to suggest that we cannot well testify too much honour for our visitor Ananda, seeing that he is the only apostle of Buddha with whose company we are likely ever to be indulged?
10095-8{_}845{_}Wherefore I would propose that neither Kammuragha nor Damburanana be assigned for his residence, but that the amenities of all the two hundred and forty-four thousand hells be combined in a new one, constructed especially for his reception."
10095-8{_}846{_}The imp having thus spoken, the senior demons were amazed at his precocity, and performed a _pradakshina_, exclaiming, "Truly thou art a highly superior young devil!"
10095-8{_}847{_}They then departed to  prepare the new infernal chamber, agreeably to his recipe.
10095-8{_}848{_}Ananda awoke, shuddering with terror.
10095-8{_}849{_}"Why," he exclaimed, "why was I ever an apostle?
10095-8{_}850{_}O Buddha!
10095-8{_}851{_}Buddha!
10095-8{_}852{_}how hard are the paths of saintliness!
10095-8{_}853{_}How prone to error are the well-meaning!
10095-8{_}854{_}How huge is the absurdity of spiritual pride!"
10095-8{_}855{_}"Thou hast discovered that, my son?"
10095-8{_}856{_}said a gentle voice in his vicinity.
10095-8{_}857{_}He turned and beheld the divine Buddha, radiant with a mild and benignant light.
10095-8{_}858{_}A cloud seemed rolled away from his vision, and he recognised in his master the Glendoveer, the Jogi, and the Physician.
10095-8{_}859{_}"O holy teacher!"
10095-8{_}860{_}exclaimed he in extreme perturbation, "whither shall I turn?
10095-8{_}861{_}My sin forbids me to approach thee."
10095-8{_}862{_}"Not on account of thy sin art thou forbidden, my son," returned Buddha, "but on account of the ridiculous and unsavoury plight to which thy knavery and disobedience have reduced thee.
10095-8{_}863{_}I have now appeared to remind thee that this day all my apostles meet on Mount Vindhya to render an account of their mission, and to inquire whether I am to deliver thine in thy stead, or whether thou art minded to proclaim it thyself."
10095-8{_}864{_}"I will render it with my own lips," resolutely exclaimed Ananda.
10095-8{_}865{_}"It is meet that I should bear the humiliation of acknowledging my folly."
10095-8{_}866{_}"Thou hast said well, my son," replied Buddha, "and in return I will permit thee to discard the attire, if such it may be termed, of a Jogi, and to appear in our assembly wearing the yellow robe as beseems my disciple.
10095-8{_}867{_}Nay, I will even infringe  my own rule on thy behalf, and perform a not inconsiderable miracle by immediately transporting thee to the summit of Vindhya, where the faithful are already beginning to assemble.
10095-8{_}868{_}Thou wouldst otherwise incur much risk of being torn to pieces by the multitude, who, as the shouts now approaching may instruct thee, are beginning to extirpate my religion at the instigation of the new king, thy hopeful pupil.
10095-8{_}869{_}The old king is dead, poisoned by the Brahmins."
10095-8{_}870{_}"O master!
10095-8{_}871{_}master!"
10095-8{_}872{_}exclaimed Ananda, weeping bitterly, "and is all the work undone, and all by my fault and folly?"
10095-8{_}873{_}"That which is built on fraud and imposture can by no means endure," returned Buddha, "be it the very truth of Heaven.
10095-8{_}874{_}Be comforted; thou shalt proclaim my doctrine to better purpose in other lands.
10095-8{_}875{_}Thou hast this time but a sorry account to render of thy stewardship; yet thou mayest truly declare that thou hast obeyed my precept in the letter, if not in the spirit, since none can assert that thou hast ever wrought any miracle."
10095-8{_}876{_}THE CITY OF PHILOSOPHERS    I   Nature is manifold, not infinite, though the extent of the resources of which she can dispose almost enables her to pass for such.
10095-8{_}877{_}Her cards are so multitudinous that the pairs are easily shuffled into ages so far asunder that their resemblance escapes remark.
10095-8{_}878{_}But sometimes her mischievous daughter Fortune manages to thrust these duplicates into such conspicuous places that their similarity cannot pass unobserved, and Nature is caught plagiarising from herself.
10095-8{_}879{_}She is thus detected dealing a king--or knave--a second time in the person of a king who has already fallen from her pack as an emperor.
10095-8{_}880{_}Brilliant, careless, selfish, yet good-natured _vauriens_, the Roman Emperor Gallienus and our Charles the Second excelled in every art save the art of reigning, and might have excelled in that also if they would have taken the trouble.
10095-8{_}881{_}The circumstances of their reigns were in many respects as similar as their characters.
10095-8{_}882{_}Both were the sons of grave and strict fathers, each of whom had met with terrible misfortunes: one deprived of his liberty by his enemies, the other of his head by his own subjects.
10095-8{_}883{_}Each of the sons had been grievously vexed by rebels, but Charles's troubles from this quarter had mostly ended where those  of Gallienus began.
10095-8{_}884{_}Each saw his dominions ravaged by pestilence in a manner beyond all former experience.
10095-8{_}885{_}The Goths destroyed the temple of the Ephesian Diana, and the Dutch burned the English fleet at Chatham.
10095-8{_}886{_}Charles shut up the Exchequer, and Gallienus debased the coinage.
10095-8{_}887{_}Charles accepted a pension from Louis XIV., and Gallienus devolved the burden of his Eastern provinces on a Syrian Emir.
10095-8{_}888{_}Their tastes and pursuits were as similar as their histories.
10095-8{_}889{_}Charles excelled as a wit and a critic; Gallienus as a poet and a gastronomer.
10095-8{_}890{_}Charles was curious about chemistry, and founded the Royal Society.
10095-8{_}891{_}In the third century the conception of the systematic investigation of nature did not exist.
10095-8{_}892{_}Gallienus, therefore, could not patronise exact science; and the great literary light of the age, Longinus, irradiated the court of Palmyra.
10095-8{_}893{_}But the Emperor bestowed his favour in ample measure on the chief contemporary philosopher, Plotinus, who strove to unite the characters of Plato and Pythagoras, of sage and seer.
10095-8{_}894{_}Like Schelling in time to come, he maintained the necessity of a special organ for the apprehension of philosophy, without perceiving that he thereby proclaimed philosophy bankrupt, and placed himself on the level of the Oriental hierophants, with whose sublime quackeries the modest sage could not hope to contend.
10095-8{_}895{_}So extreme was his humility, that he would not claim to have been consciously united to the Divinity more than four times in his life; without condemning magic and thaumaturgy, he left their practice to more adventurous spirits, and contented himself with the occasional visits of a  familiar demon in the shape of a serpent.
10095-8{_}896{_}He experienced, however, frequent visitations of trance or ecstasy, sometimes lasting for a long period; and it may have been in one of these that he was inspired by the idea of asking the Emperor for a decayed city in Campania, there to establish a philosophic commonwealth as nearly upon the model of Plato's Republic as the degeneracy of the times would allow.
10095-8{_}897{_}"I cannot," said Gallienus, when the project had been explained to him, "object in principle to aught so festive and jocose.
10095-8{_}898{_}The age is turned upside down; its comedians are lamentable, and its sages ludicrous.
10095-8{_}899{_}It must moreover, I apprehend, be sated with the earthquakes, famines, pestilences, and barbarian invasions with which it hath been exclusively regaled for so long, and must crave something enlivening, of the nature of thy proposition.
10095-8{_}900{_}But whether, when we arrive at the consideration of ways and means, I shall find my interview with my treasurer enlivening, is gravely to be questioned.
10095-8{_}901{_}I have heard homilies enough on my prodigality, which merely means that I prefer spending my treasures on myself to saving them for my successor, whose title will probably have been acquired by cutting my throat."
10095-8{_}902{_}"I know," said Plotinus, "that the expenses of administering an empire must necessarily be prodigious.
10095-8{_}903{_}I am aware that the principal generals are only kept to their allegiance by enormous bribes.
10095-8{_}904{_}I well understand that the Empress must have pearls, and that the Roman populace must have panthers; and that, since Egypt has revolted, the hippopotamus is worth his weight in gold.
10095-8{_}905{_}I am further aware that the proposed  colossal statue of your Majesty in the same metal, including a staircase, with room in the head for a child, like another Pallas in the brain of Zeus, must alone involve very considerable outlay.
10095-8{_}906{_}But I am encouraged by your Majesty's wise and statesmanlike measure of debasing the currency; since, money having become devoid of value, there can be no difficulty in devoting any amount of it to any purpose required."
10095-8{_}907{_}"Plotinus," said Gallienus, "in this age the devil is taking the hindmost, and we are the hindmost.
10095-8{_}908{_}There are tidings to-day of a new earthquake in Bithynia, and three days' darkness, also of outbreaks of pestilence, and incursions of the barbarians, too numerous as well as too disagreeable to mention.
10095-8{_}909{_}At this moment some revolted legion is probably forcing the purple upon some reluctant general; and the Persian king, a great equestrian, is doubtless mounting his horse by the aid of my father's back.
10095-8{_}910{_}If I had been an old Roman, I should by this time have avenged my father, but I am a man of my age.
10095-8{_}911{_}Take the money for thy city, and see that it yields me some amusement at any rate.
10095-8{_}912{_}I assume, of course, that thou wilt exercise severe economy, and that cresses and spring water will be the diet of thy philosophers.
10095-8{_}913{_}Farewell, I go to Gaul to encounter Postumus.
10095-8{_}914{_}Willingly would I leave him in peace in Gaul if he would leave me in peace in Italy; but I foresee that if I do not attack him there he will attack me here.
10095-8{_}915{_}As if the Empire were not large enough for us all!
10095-8{_}916{_}What an ass the fellow must be!"
10095-8{_}917{_}And so Gallienus changed his silk for steel, and departed for his Gallic campaign, where he bore  himself more stoutly than his light talk would have led those who judged him by it to expect.
10095-8{_}918{_}Plotinus, provided with an Imperial rescript, undertook the regulation of his philosophical commonwealth in Campania, where a brief experience of architects and sophists threw him into an ecstasy, not of joy, which endured an unusually long time.
10095-8{_}919{_}II   On awakening from his long trance, Plotinus's first sensation was one of bodily hunger, the second of an even keener appetite for news of his philosophical Republic.
10095-8{_}920{_}In both respects it promised well to perceive that his chamber was occupied by his most eminent scholar, Porphyry, though he was less gratified to observe his disciple busied, instead of with the scrolls of the sages, with an enormous roll of accounts, which appeared to be occasioning him much perplexity.
10095-8{_}921{_}"Porphyry!"
10095-8{_}922{_}cried the master, and the faithful disciple was by his couch in a moment.
10095-8{_}923{_}We pass over the mutual joy, the greetings, the administration of restoratives and creature comforts, the eager interrogations of Porphyry respecting the things his master had heard and seen in his trance, which proved to be unspeakable.
10095-8{_}924{_}"And now," said Plotinus, who with all his mysticism was so good a man of business that, as his biographers acquaint us, he was in special request as a trustee, "and now, concerning this roll of thine.
10095-8{_}925{_}Is it possible that the accounts connected with the installation of a few abstemious  lovers of wisdom can have swollen to such a prodigous bulk?
10095-8{_}926{_}But indeed, why few?
10095-8{_}927{_}Peradventure all the philosophers of the earth have flocked to my city."
10095-8{_}928{_}"It has, indeed," said Porphyry evasively, "been found necessary to incur certain expenses not originally foreseen."
10095-8{_}929{_}"For a library, perhaps?"
10095-8{_}930{_}inquired Plotinus.
10095-8{_}931{_}"I remember thinking, just before my ecstasy, that the scrolls of the divine Plato, many of them autographic, might require some special housing."
10095-8{_}932{_}"I rejoice to state," rejoined Porphyry, "that it is not these volumes that have involved us in our present difficulties with the superintendent of the Imperial treasury, nor can they indeed, seeing that they are now impignorated with him."
10095-8{_}933{_}"Plato's manuscripts pawned!"
10095-8{_}934{_}exclaimed Plotinus, aghast.
10095-8{_}935{_}"Wherefore?"
10095-8{_}936{_}"As part collateral security for expenses incurred on behalf of objects deemed of more importance by the majority of the philosophers."
10095-8{_}937{_}"For example?"
10095-8{_}938{_}"Repairing bath and completing amphitheatre."
10095-8{_}939{_}"Bath!
10095-8{_}940{_}Amphitheatre!"
10095-8{_}941{_}gasped Plotinus.
10095-8{_}942{_}"O dear master," remonstrated Porphyry, "thou didst not deem that philosophers could be induced to settle in a spot devoid of these necessaries?
10095-8{_}943{_}Not a single one would have stayed if I had not yielded to their demands, which, as regarded the bath, involved the addition of exedrae and of a sphaeristerium."
10095-8{_}944{_}"And what can they want with an amphitheatre?"
10095-8{_}945{_}groaned Plotinus.
10095-8{_}946{_}"They _say_ it is for lectures," replied Porphyry; "I trust there is no truth in the rumour that the head of the Stoics is three parts owner of a lion of singular ferocity."
10095-8{_}947{_}"I must see to this as soon as I can get about," said Plotinus, turning to the accounts.
10095-8{_}948{_}"What's this?
10095-8{_}949{_}To couch and litter for head of Peripatetic school!"
10095-8{_}950{_}"Who is so enormously fat," explained Porphyry, "that these conveniences are really indispensable to him.
10095-8{_}951{_}The Peripatetic school is positively at a standstill."
10095-8{_}952{_}"And no great matter," said Plotinus; "its master Aristotle was at best a rationalist, without perception of the supersensual.
10095-8{_}953{_}What's this?
10095-8{_}954{_}To Maximus, for the invocation of demons."
10095-8{_}955{_}"That," said Porphyry, "is our own Platonic dirty linen, and I heartily wish we were washing it elsewhere.
10095-8{_}956{_}Thou must know, dear master, that during thy trance the theurgic movement has attained a singular development, and that thou art regarded with disdain by thy younger disciples as one wholly behind the age, unacquainted with the higher magic, and who can produce no other outward and visible token of the Divine favour than the occasional companionship of a serpent."
10095-8{_}957{_}"I would not assert that theurgy may not be lawfully undertaken," replied Plotinus, "provided that the adept shall have purified himself by a fast of forty months."
10095-8{_}958{_}"It may be from neglect of this precaution," said Porphyry, "that our Maximus finds it so much easier to evoke the shades of Commodus and Caracalla than those of Socrates and Marcus Aurelius; and that these good spirits, when they do come, have no more recondite information to  convey than that virtue differs from vice, and that one's grandmother is a fitting object of reverence."
10095-8{_}959{_}"I fear this must expose Platonic truth to the derision of Epicurean scoffers," remarked Plotinus.
10095-8{_}960{_}"O master, speak not of Epicureans, still less of Stoics!
10095-8{_}961{_}Wait till thou hast regained thy full strength, and then take counsel of some oracle."
10095-8{_}962{_}"What meanest thou?"
10095-8{_}963{_}exclaimed Plotinus, "I insist upon knowing."
10095-8{_}964{_}Porphyry was saved from replying by the hasty entrance of a bustling portly personage of loud voice and imperious manner, in whom Plotinus recognised Theocles, the chief of the Stoics.
10095-8{_}965{_}"I rejoice, Plotinus," he began, "that thou hast at length emerged from that condition of torpor, so unworthy of a philosopher, which I might well designate as charlatanism were I not so firmly determined to speak no word which can offend any man.
10095-8{_}966{_}Thou wilt now be able to reprehend the malice or obtuseness of thy deputy, and to do me right in my contention with these impure dogs."
10095-8{_}967{_}"Which be they?"
10095-8{_}968{_}asked Plotinus.
10095-8{_}969{_}"Do I not sufficiently indicate the followers of Epicurus?"
10095-8{_}970{_}demanded the Stoic.
10095-8{_}971{_}"O master," explained Porphyry, "in allotting and fitting up apartments designed for the respective sects of philosophers I naturally gave heed to what I understood to be the principles of each.
10095-8{_}972{_}To the Epicureans, as lovers of pleasure and luxury, I assigned the most commodious quarters, furnished the same with soft cushions and costly hangings, and provided a liberal table.
10095-8{_}973{_}I should have deemed it insulting to have offered any of these things to the frugal followers of Zeno, and nothing can surpass my astonishment at the manner in which the austere Theocles has incessantly persecuted me for choice food and wine, stately rooms and soft couches."
10095-8{_}974{_}"O Plotinus," replied Theocles, "let me make the grounds of my conduct clear to thee.
10095-8{_}975{_}In the first place, the honour of my school is in my keeping.
10095-8{_}976{_}What will the vulgar think when they see the sty of Epicurus sumptuously adorned, and the porch of Zeno shabby and bare?
10095-8{_}977{_}Will they not deem that the Epicureans are highly respected and the Stoics made of little account?
10095-8{_}978{_}Furthermore, how can I and my disciples manifest our contempt for gold, dainties, wine, fine linen, and all the other instruments of luxury, unless we have them to despise?
10095-8{_}979{_}Shall we not appear like foxes, vilipending the grapes that we cannot reach?
10095-8{_}980{_}Not so; offer me delicacies that I may reject them, wine that I may pour it into the kennel, Tyrian purple that I may trample upon it, gold that I may fling it away; if it break an Epicurean's head, so much the better."
10095-8{_}981{_}"Plotinus," said Hermon, the chief of the Epicureans, who had meanwhile entered the apartment, "let this hypocrite have what he wants, and send him away.
10095-8{_}982{_}I and my followers are perfectly willing to remove at once into the inferior apartments, and leave ours for his occupation with all their furniture, and the reversion of our bill of fare.
10095-8{_}983{_}Thou should'st know that the imputations of the vulgar against our sect are the grossest calumnies.
10095-8{_}984{_}The Epicurean places happiness in tranquil enjoyment, not in luxury or sensual pleasures.
10095-8{_}985{_}There is not a thing I possess  which I am not perfectly willing to resign, except the society of my female disciple."
10095-8{_}986{_}"Thy female disciple!"
10095-8{_}987{_}exclaimed the horrified Plotinus.
10095-8{_}988{_}"Thou art worse than the Stoic!"
10095-8{_}989{_}"Plotinus," said the Epicurean, "consider well ere, as is the manner of Platonists, thou committest thyself to a proposition of a transparently foolish nature.
10095-8{_}990{_}Thou desirest to gather all sorts of philosophers around thee, but to what end, if they are restrained from manifesting their characteristic tenets?
10095-8{_}991{_}Thou mightest as well seek to illustrate the habits of animals by establishing a menagerie in which panthers should eat grass, and antelopes be dieted on rabbits.
10095-8{_}992{_}An Epicurean without his female companion, unless by his own choice, is no more an Epicurean than a Cynic is a Cynic without his rags and his impudence.
10095-8{_}993{_}Wilt thou take from me my Pannychis, an object pleasing to the eye, and leave yonder fellow his tatters and his vermin?"
10095-8{_}994{_}The apartment had gradually filled with philosophers, and Hermon was pointing to a follower of Diogenes whose robe so fully bespoke his obedience to his master's precepts that his skin seemed almost clean in comparison.
10095-8{_}995{_}"Consider also," continued the Epicurean, "that thou art thyself by no means exempt from scandal."
10095-8{_}996{_}"What does the man mean?"
10095-8{_}997{_}demanded Plotinus, turning to Porphyry.
10095-8{_}998{_}"Get them away," whispered the disciple, "and I will tell thee."
10095-8{_}999{_}Plotinus hastily conceded the point raised with reference to the interesting Pannychis, and the  philosophers went off to effect their exchange of quarters.
10095-8{_}1000{_}As soon as the room was clear, he repeated:  "What _does_ the man mean?"
10095-8{_}1001{_}"I suppose he is thinking of Leaena," said Porphyry.
10095-8{_}1002{_}"The most notorious character in Rome, who, finding her charms on the wane, has lately betaken herself to philosophy?"
10095-8{_}1003{_}"The same."
10095-8{_}1004{_}"What of her?"
10095-8{_}1005{_}"She has followed thee here.
10095-8{_}1006{_}She affects the greatest devotion to thee.
10095-8{_}1007{_}She vows that nothing shall make her budge until thou hast recovered from thy ecstasy, and admitted her as thy disciple.
10095-8{_}1008{_}She has rejected numerous overtures from the philosopher Theocles; entirely for thy sake, she affirms.
10095-8{_}1009{_}She comes three times a day to inquire respecting thy condition, and I fear it must be acknowledged that she has once or twice managed to get into thy chamber."
10095-8{_}1010{_}"O ye immortal Gods!"
10095-8{_}1011{_}groaned Plotinus.
10095-8{_}1012{_}"Here she is!"
10095-8{_}1013{_}exclaimed Porphyry, as a woman of masculine stature and bearing, with the remains of beauty not unskilfully patched, forced an entrance into the room.
10095-8{_}1014{_}"Plotinus," she exclaimed, "behold the most impassioned of thy disciples.
10095-8{_}1015{_}Let us celebrate the mystic nuptials of Wisdom and Beauty.
10095-8{_}1016{_}Let the claims of my sex to philosophic distinction be vindicated in my person."
10095-8{_}1017{_}"The question of the admission of women to share the studies and society of men," rejoined Plotinus, "is one by no means exempt from difficulty."
10095-8{_}1018{_}"How so?
10095-8{_}1019{_}I deemed it had been determined long ago in favour of Aspasia?"
10095-8{_}1020{_}"Aspasia," said Plotinus, "was a very exceptional woman."
10095-8{_}1021{_}"And am not I?"
10095-8{_}1022{_}"I hope, that is, I conceive so," said Plotinus.
10095-8{_}1023{_}"But one may be an exceptional woman without being an Aspasia."
10095-8{_}1024{_}"How so?
10095-8{_}1025{_}Am I inferior to Aspasia in beauty?"
10095-8{_}1026{_}"I should hope not," said Plotinus ambiguously.
10095-8{_}1027{_}"Or in the irregularity of my deportment?"
10095-8{_}1028{_}"I should think not," said Plotinus, with more confidence.
10095-8{_}1029{_}"Then why does the Plato of our age hesitate to welcome his Diotima?"
10095-8{_}1030{_}"Because," said Plotinus, "you are not Diotima, and I am not Plato."
10095-8{_}1031{_}"I am sure I am as much like Diotima as you are like Plato," retorted the lady.
10095-8{_}1032{_}"But let us come to our own time.
10095-8{_}1033{_}Do I not hear that that creature Pannychis has obtained the freedom of the philosophers' city, and the right to study therein?"
10095-8{_}1034{_}"She takes private lessons from Hermon, who is responsible for her."
10095-8{_}1035{_}"The very thing!"
10095-8{_}1036{_}exclaimed Leaena triumphantly.
10095-8{_}1037{_}"I take private lessons from thee, and thou art responsible for me.
10095-8{_}1038{_}Venus!
10095-8{_}1039{_}what's that?"
10095-8{_}1040{_}The exclamation was prompted by the sudden appearance of an enormous serpent, which, emerging from a chink in the wall, glided swiftly towards the couch of Plotinus.
10095-8{_}1041{_}He reached forward to greet it, uttering a cry of pleasure.
10095-8{_}1042{_}"My guardian, my tutelary dæmon," he exclaimed, "visible manifestation of Æsculapius!
10095-8{_}1043{_}Then I am not forsaken by the immortal gods."
10095-8{_}1044{_}"Take away the monster," cried Leaena, in violent agitation, "the nasty thing!
10095-8{_}1045{_}Plotinus, how can you?
10095-8{_}1046{_}Oh, I shall faint!
10095-8{_}1047{_}I shall die!
10095-8{_}1048{_}Take it away, I say.
10095-8{_}1049{_}You must choose between it and me."
10095-8{_}1050{_}"Then, Madam," said Plotinus, civilly but firmly, "I choose _it_."
10095-8{_}1051{_}"Thank Æsculapius we are rid of her," he added, as Leaena vanished from the apartment.
10095-8{_}1052{_}"I wish I knew that," said Porphyry.
10095-8{_}1053{_}And indeed after no long time a note came up from Theocles, who was sure that Plotinus would not refuse him that privilege of instructing a female disciple which had been already, with such manifest advantage to philosophical research, accorded to his colleague Hermon.
10095-8{_}1054{_}No objection could well be made, especially as Plotinus did not foresee how many chambermaids, and pages, and cooks, and perfumers, and tiring women and bath attendants would be required, ere Leaena could feel herself moderately comfortable.
10095-8{_}1055{_}How unlike the modest Pannychis!
10095-8{_}1056{_}who wanted but half a bed, which need not be stuffed with the down of hares or the feathers of partridges, without which sleep refused to visit Leaena's eyelids.
10095-8{_}1057{_}It was natural that Plotinus should appeal to Gallienus, now returned from the Gallic expedition, but he could extract nothing save mysterious intimations that the Emperor had his eye upon the philosophers, and that they might find him among  them when they least expected it.
10095-8{_}1058{_}Plotinus's spirits drooped, and Porphyry was almost glad when he again relapsed into an ecstasy.
10095-8{_}1059{_}III   When Plotinus's eyes were at length opened, they fell not this time upon the faithful Porphyry, but upon two youthful followers of Plato who were beguiling the tedium of their vigil at his bedside by a game of dice, which prevented their observing his resuscitation.
10095-8{_}1060{_}After a moment's hesitation Plotinus resolved to lie quiet in the hopes of hearing something that might indicate what influences were in the ascendant in the philosophical republic.
10095-8{_}1061{_}He had not long to wait.
10095-8{_}1062{_}"Dice is dull work for long," said one of the young men, indolently throwing himself back, and letting his caster fall upon the floor.
10095-8{_}1063{_}"To think how much better one might be employed, but for having to watch this old fool here!
10095-8{_}1064{_}I've a great mind to call up a slave."
10095-8{_}1065{_}"All the slaves are sure to have gone to the show, unless any of them should be Christians.
10095-8{_}1066{_}Besides, Porphyry would hear you, he's only in a cat's sleep," returned his companion.
10095-8{_}1067{_}"Well, I mean to say it's a shame.
10095-8{_}1068{_}All the town will be in the theatre by this time."
10095-8{_}1069{_}"How many gladiators, said you?"
10095-8{_}1070{_}"Forty pairs, the best show Campania has seen time out of mind."
10095-8{_}1071{_}"How has it all come about?"
10095-8{_}1072{_}"Oh, news comes of the death of Postumus, killed by his own soldiers, and this passes as a  great victory for want of a better, 'We must have a day of thanksgiving,' says Theocles.
10095-8{_}1073{_}'Right,' says Leaena, 'I am dying to see an exhibition of gladiators.'
10095-8{_}1074{_}Theocles demurs at first, expecting to have to find the money--but Leaena tugs at his beard, and he gives in.
10095-8{_}1075{_}Just at the nick of time the right sort of fellow pops up nobody knows whence, a lanista with hair like curling helichryse, as Theocritus has it, and a small army of gladiators, whom, out of devotion to the Emperor, he offers to exhibit for nothing.
10095-8{_}1076{_}Who so pleased as Theocles now?
10095-8{_}1077{_}He takes the chair as archon with Leaena by his side, and off goes every soul in the place, except Pannychis, who cannot bear the sight of blood, and Porphyry, who is an outrageous humanitarian, and us poor devils left in charge of this old dreamer."
10095-8{_}1078{_}"Couldn't we leave him to mind himself?
10095-8{_}1079{_}He isn't likely to awake yet."
10095-8{_}1080{_}"Try him with your cloak-pin."
10095-8{_}1081{_}The student detached the implement in question, which was about the size of a small stiletto.
10095-8{_}1082{_}Feeling uncertain what part of his person was to be the subject of experiment, Plotinus judged it advisable to manifest his recovery in an unmistakable fashion.
10095-8{_}1083{_}"O dear Master, what joy!"
10095-8{_}1084{_}cried both the students in a breath.
10095-8{_}1085{_}"Porphyry!
10095-8{_}1086{_}Porphyry!"
10095-8{_}1087{_}The trusty scholar appeared immediately, and under pretence of fetching food, the two neophytes eloped to the amphitheatre.
10095-8{_}1088{_}"What means all this, Porphyry?"
10095-8{_}1089{_}demanded Plotinus sternly.
10095-8{_}1090{_}"The City of Philosophers polluted by human blood!
10095-8{_}1091{_}The lovers of wisdom mingling with the dregs of the rabble!"
10095-8{_}1092{_}Porphyry's account, which Plotinus could only extract by consenting to eat while his disciple talked, corresponded in all essential particulars with that of the two young men.
10095-8{_}1093{_}"And I see not," added he, "what we can do in the matter.
10095-8{_}1094{_}This abomination is supposed to be in honour of the Emperor's victories.
10095-8{_}1095{_}If we interfere with it we shall be executed as rebels, supposing that we are not first torn to pieces as rioters."
10095-8{_}1096{_}"Porphyry," replied Plotinus, "I should esteem this disgrace to philosophy a disgrace to myself if I did not my utmost to avert it.
10095-8{_}1097{_}Remain thou here, and perform my funeral rites if it be necessary."
10095-8{_}1098{_}But to this Porphyry would by no means consent, and the two philosophers proceeded to the amphitheatre together.
10095-8{_}1099{_}It was so crowded that there was no room on the seats for another person.
10095-8{_}1100{_}Theocles was enthroned in the chair of honour, his beard manifesting evident traces of the depilatories administered by Leaena, who nevertheless sat by his side, her voluptuous face gloating over the anticipated banquet of agony.
10095-8{_}1101{_}The philosophic part of the spectators were ranged all around, the remaining seats were occupied by a miscellaneous public.
10095-8{_}1102{_}The master of the gladiators, a man of distinguished appearance, whose yellow locks gave him the aspect of a barbarian prince, stood in the arena surrounded by his myrmidons.
10095-8{_}1103{_}The entry of Plotinus and Porphyry attracted his attention: he motioned to his followers, and in an instant the philosophers were seized, bound, and gagged without the excited assembly being in the least conscious of their presence.
10095-8{_}1104{_}Two men stepped out into the arena, both fine and attractive figures.
10095-8{_}1105{_}The athletic limbs, the fair complexion, the curling yellow hair of one proclaimed the Goth; he lightly swung his huge sword in his right hand, and looked as if his sole arm would easily put to flight the crowd of effeminate spectators.
10095-8{_}1106{_}The other's beauty was of another sort; young, slender, pensive, spiritual, he looked like anything rather than a gladiator, and held his downward pointed sword with a negligent grasp.
10095-8{_}1107{_}"Guard thyself!"
10095-8{_}1108{_}cried the Goth, placing himself in an attitude of offence.
10095-8{_}1109{_}"I spill not the blood of a fellow-creature," answered the other, casting his sword away from him.
10095-8{_}1110{_}"Coward!"
10095-8{_}1111{_}yelled well-nigh every voice in the amphitheatre.
10095-8{_}1112{_}"No," answered the youth with a grave smile, "Christian."
10095-8{_}1113{_}His shield and helmet followed his sword, he stood entirely defenceless before his adversary.
10095-8{_}1114{_}"Throw him to my lion," cried Theocles.
10095-8{_}1115{_}"Or thy lioness," suggested Hermon.
10095-8{_}1116{_}This allusion to Leaena provoked a burst of laughter.
10095-8{_}1117{_}Suddenly the Goth aimed a mighty blow at the head of the unresisting man.
10095-8{_}1118{_}A shorn curl fell to the ground, the consummate skill of the swordsman averted all further contact between his blade and the Christian, who remained erect and smiling, without having moved a muscle or an eyelash.
10095-8{_}1119{_}"Master," said the Goth, addressing the lanista, "I had rather fight ten armed men than this unarmed one."
10095-8{_}1120{_}"Good," returned his lord, with a gesture of approval.
10095-8{_}1121{_}"Retire both of you."
10095-8{_}1122{_}A roar of disapprobation broke out from the spectators, which seemed not to produce the slightest effect on the lanista.
10095-8{_}1123{_}"Turn out the next pair," they cried.
10095-8{_}1124{_}"I shall not," said he.
10095-8{_}1125{_}"Wherefore?"
10095-8{_}1126{_}"Because I do not choose."
10095-8{_}1127{_}"Rogue!
10095-8{_}1128{_}Cheat!
10095-8{_}1129{_}Swindler!
10095-8{_}1130{_}Cast him into prison!
10095-8{_}1131{_}Throw him to the lion!"
10095-8{_}1132{_}Such epithets and recommendations rained from the spectators' seats, accompanied by a pelting of more substantial missiles.
10095-8{_}1133{_}In an instant the yellow hair and common dress lay on the ground, and those who knew him not by the features could by the Imperial ornaments recognise the Emperor Gallienus.
10095-8{_}1134{_}With no less celerity his followers, the Goth and the Christian excepted, disencumbered themselves of their exterior vesture, and stood forward in the character of Roman soldiers.
10095-8{_}1135{_}"Friends," cried Gallienus, turning to the plebeian multitude, "I am not about to balk you of your sport."
10095-8{_}1136{_}At a sign from him the legionaries ascended to the seats allotted to the philosophic portion of the audience, and a torrent of wisdom in their persons, including that of Leaena, flung forth with the energy of a catapult, descended abruptly and violently to the earth.
10095-8{_}1137{_}They were instantly seized and dragged into an erect attitude by the remainder of the soldiery, who, amid the most tempestuous peals of laughter and applause from the delighted public, thrust swords into their hands, ranged them in opposite ranks, and summoned  them to begin the fight and quit themselves like men.
10095-8{_}1138{_}It was equally ludicrous and pitiable to see the bald, mostly grey-bearded men, their garments torn in their expulsion and their persons bruised by the fall, confronting each other with quaking limbs, helplessly brandishing their weapons or feebly calling their adversaries to come on, while the soldiers prodded them from behind with spears, and urged them into the close quarters they so anxiously desired to avoid.
10095-8{_}1139{_}Plotinus, helpless with his bonds and gag, looked on in impotent horror.
10095-8{_}1140{_}Gallienus was often cruel, but could he intend such a revolting massacre?
10095-8{_}1141{_}There must be something behind.
10095-8{_}1142{_}The honour of developing the Emperor's purpose was reserved for Theocles, who, with admirable presence of mind, had ever since he found he must fight been engaged in trying to select the weakest antagonist.
10095-8{_}1143{_}After hesitating between the unwieldy chief of the Peripatetics and the feminine Leaena he fixed on the latter, partly moved, perhaps, by the hope of avenging his beard.
10095-8{_}1144{_}With a martial cry he sprang towards her, and upraised his weapon for a swashing blow.
10095-8{_}1145{_}But he had sadly miscalculated.
10095-8{_}1146{_}Leaena was hardly less versed in the combats of Mars than in those of Venus, having, in fact, commenced her distinguished career as a camp-follower of the Emperor Gordian.
10095-8{_}1147{_}A tremendous stroke caught him on the hand; his blade dropped to the earth; why did not the fingers follow?
10095-8{_}1148{_}Leaena elucidated the problem by a still more violent blow on his face; torrents of blood gushed forth indeed, but only from the nose.
10095-8{_}1149{_}The sword doubled up; it had neither point nor edge.
10095-8{_}1150{_}Encouraged by this  opportune discovery the philosophers attacked each other with infinite spirit and valour.
10095-8{_}1151{_}Infuriated by the blows given and received, by the pokings and proddings of the military, and the hilarious derision of the public, they cast away the shivered blades and resorted to the weapons of Nature.
10095-8{_}1152{_}They kicked, they cuffed, they scratched, they tore the garments from each other's shoulders, they foamed and rolled gasping in the yellow sand of the arena.
10095-8{_}1153{_}At a signal from the Emperor the portal of the amphitheatre was thrown open, and the whole mass of clawing and cuffing philosophy was bundled ignominiously into the street.
10095-8{_}1154{_}By this time Gallienus was seated on his tribunal, and Plotinus, released from his bonds, was standing by his side.
10095-8{_}1155{_}"O Emperor," he murmured, deeply abashed, "what can I urge?
10095-8{_}1156{_}Thou wilt surely demolish my city!"
10095-8{_}1157{_}"No, Plotinus," replied Gallienus, pointing to the Goth and the Christian, "there are the men who will destroy the City of Philosophers.
10095-8{_}1158{_}Would that were all they will destroy!"
10095-8{_}1159{_}THE DEMON POPE   "So you won't sell me your soul?"
10095-8{_}1160{_}said the devil.
10095-8{_}1161{_}"Thank you," replied the student, "I had rather keep it myself, if it's all the same to you."
10095-8{_}1162{_}"But it's not all the same to me.
10095-8{_}1163{_}I want it very particularly.
10095-8{_}1164{_}Come, I'll be liberal.
10095-8{_}1165{_}I said twenty years.
10095-8{_}1166{_}You can have thirty."
10095-8{_}1167{_}The student shook his head.
10095-8{_}1168{_}"Forty!"
10095-8{_}1169{_}Another shake.
10095-8{_}1170{_}"Fifty!"
10095-8{_}1171{_}As before.
10095-8{_}1172{_}"Now," said the devil, "I know I'm going to do a foolish thing, but I cannot bear to see a clever, spirited young man throw himself away.
10095-8{_}1173{_}I'll make you another kind of offer.
10095-8{_}1174{_}We won't have any bargain at present, but I will push you on in the world for the next forty years.
10095-8{_}1175{_}This day forty years I come back and ask you for a boon; not your soul, mind, or anything not perfectly in your power to grant.
10095-8{_}1176{_}If you give it, we are quits; if not, I fly away with you.
10095-8{_}1177{_}What say you to this?"
10095-8{_}1178{_}The student reflected for some minutes.
10095-8{_}1179{_}"Agreed," he said at last.
10095-8{_}1180{_}Scarcely had the devil disappeared, which he did instantaneously, ere a messenger reined in his  smoking steed at the gate of the University of Cordova (the judicious reader will already have remarked that Lucifer could never have been allowed inside a Christian seat of learning), and, inquiring for the student Gerbert, presented him with the Emperor Otho's nomination to the Abbacy of Bobbio, in consideration, said the document, of his virtue and learning, well-nigh miraculous in one so young.
10095-8{_}1181{_}Such messengers were frequent visitors during Gerbert's prosperous career.
10095-8{_}1182{_}Abbot, bishop, archbishop, cardinal, he was ultimately enthroned Pope on April 2, 999, and assumed the appellation of Silvester the Second.
10095-8{_}1183{_}It was then a general belief that the world would come to an end in the following year, a catastrophe which to many seemed the more imminent from the election of a chief pastor whose celebrity as a theologian, though not inconsiderable, by no means equalled his reputation as a necromancer.
10095-8{_}1184{_}The world, notwithstanding, revolved scatheless through the dreaded twelvemonth, and early in the first year of the eleventh century Gerbert was sitting peacefully in his study, perusing a book of magic.
10095-8{_}1185{_}Volumes of algebra, astrology, alchemy, Aristotelian philosophy, and other such light reading filled his bookcase; and on a table stood an improved clock of his invention, next to his introduction of the Arabic numerals his chief legacy to posterity.
10095-8{_}1186{_}Suddenly a sound of wings was heard, and Lucifer stood by his side.
10095-8{_}1187{_}"It is a long time," said the fiend, "since I have had the pleasure of seeing you.
10095-8{_}1188{_}I have now called to remind you of our little contract, concluded this day forty years."
10095-8{_}1189{_}"You remember," said Silvester, "that you are not to ask anything exceeding my power to perform."
10095-8{_}1190{_}"I have no such intention," said Lucifer.
10095-8{_}1191{_}"On the contrary, I am about to solicit a favour which can be bestowed by you alone.
10095-8{_}1192{_}You are Pope, I desire that you would make me a Cardinal.
10095-8{_}1193{_}"In the expectation, I presume," returned Gerbert, "of becoming Pope on the next vacancy."
10095-8{_}1194{_}"An expectation," replied Lucifer, "which I may most reasonably entertain, considering my enormous wealth, my proficiency in intrigue, and the present condition of the Sacred College."
10095-8{_}1195{_}"You would doubtless," said Gerbert, "endeavour to subvert the foundations of the Faith, and, by a course of profligacy and licentiousness, render the Holy See odious and contemptible."
10095-8{_}1196{_}"On the contrary," said the fiend, "I would extirpate heresy, and all learning and knowledge as inevitably tending thereunto.
10095-8{_}1197{_}I would suffer no man to read but the priest, and confine his reading to his breviary.
10095-8{_}1198{_}I would burn your books together with your bones on the first convenient opportunity.
10095-8{_}1199{_}I would observe an austere propriety of conduct, and be especially careful not to loosen one rivet in the tremendous yoke I was forging for the minds and consciences of mankind."
10095-8{_}1200{_}"If it be so," said Gerbert, "let's be off!"
10095-8{_}1201{_}"What!"
10095-8{_}1202{_}exclaimed Lucifer, "you are willing to accompany me to the infernal regions!"
10095-8{_}1203{_}"Assuredly, rather than be accessory to the burning of Plato and Aristotle, and give place to the darkness against which I have been contending all my life."
10095-8{_}1204{_}"Gerbert," replied the demon, "this is arrant trifling.
10095-8{_}1205{_}Know you not that no good man can enter my dominions?
10095-8{_}1206{_}that, were such a thing possible, my empire would become intolerable to me, and I should be compelled to abdicate?"
10095-8{_}1207{_}"I do know it," said Gerbert, "and hence I have been able to receive your visit with composure."
10095-8{_}1208{_}"Gerbert," said the devil, with tears in his eyes, "I put it to you--is this fair, is this honest?
10095-8{_}1209{_}I undertake to promote your interests in the world; I fulfil my promise abundantly.
10095-8{_}1210{_}You obtain through my instrumentality a position to which you could never otherwise have aspired.
10095-8{_}1211{_}Often have I had a hand in the election of a Pope, but never before have I contributed to confer the tiara on one eminent for virtue and learning.
10095-8{_}1212{_}You profit by my assistance to the full, and now take advantage of an adventitious circumstance to deprive me of my reasonable guerdon.
10095-8{_}1213{_}It is my constant experience that the good people are much more slippery than the sinners, and drive much harder bargains."
10095-8{_}1214{_}"Lucifer," answered Gerbert, "I have always sought to treat you as a gentleman, hoping that you would approve yourself such in return.
10095-8{_}1215{_}I will not inquire whether it was entirely in harmony with this character to seek to intimidate me into compliance with your demand by threatening me with a penalty which you well knew could not be enforced.
10095-8{_}1216{_}I will overlook this little irregularity, and concede even more than you have requested.
10095-8{_}1217{_}You have asked to be a Cardinal.
10095-8{_}1218{_}I will make you Pope--"  "Ha!"
10095-8{_}1219{_}exclaimed Lucifer, and an internal glow  suffused his sooty hide, as the light of a fading ember is revived by breathing upon it.
10095-8{_}1220{_}"For twelve hours," continued Gerbert.
10095-8{_}1221{_}"At the expiration of that time we will consider the matter further; and if, as I anticipate, you are more anxious to divest yourself of the Papal dignity than you were to assume it, I promise to bestow upon you any boon you may ask within my power to grant, and not plainly inconsistent with religion or morals."
10095-8{_}1222{_}"Done!"
10095-8{_}1223{_}cried the demon.
10095-8{_}1224{_}Gerbert uttered some cabalistic words, and in a moment the apartment held two Pope Silvesters, entirely indistinguishable save by their attire, and the fact that one limped slightly with the left foot.
10095-8{_}1225{_}"You will find the Pontifical apparel in this cupboard," said Gerbert, and, taking his book of magic with him, he retreated through a masked door to a secret chamber.
10095-8{_}1226{_}As the door closed behind him he chuckled, and muttered to himself, "Poor old Lucifer!
10095-8{_}1227{_}Sold again!"
10095-8{_}1228{_}If Lucifer was sold he did not seem to know it.
10095-8{_}1229{_}He approached a large slab of silver which did duty as a mirror, and contemplated his personal appearance with some dissatisfaction.
10095-8{_}1230{_}"I certainly don't look half so well without my horns," he soliloquised, "and I am sure I shall miss my tail most grievously."
10095-8{_}1231{_}A tiara and a train, however, made fair amends for the deficient appendages, and Lucifer now looked every inch a Pope.
10095-8{_}1232{_}He was about to call the master of the ceremonies, and summon a consistory, when the door was burst open, and seven cardinals, brandishing poniards, rushed into the room.
10095-8{_}1233{_}"Down with the sorcerer!"
10095-8{_}1234{_}they cried, as they seized and gagged him.
10095-8{_}1235{_}"Death to the Saracen!"
10095-8{_}1236{_}"Practises algebra, and other devilish arts!"
10095-8{_}1237{_}"Knows Greek!"
10095-8{_}1238{_}"Talks Arabic!"
10095-8{_}1239{_}"Reads Hebrew!"
10095-8{_}1240{_}"Burn him!"
10095-8{_}1241{_}"Smother him!"
10095-8{_}1242{_}"Let him be deposed by a general council," said a young and inexperienced Cardinal.
10095-8{_}1243{_}"Heaven forbid!"
10095-8{_}1244{_}said an old and wary one, _sotto voce_.
10095-8{_}1245{_}Lucifer struggled frantically, but the feeble frame he was doomed to inhabit for the next eleven hours was speedily exhausted.
10095-8{_}1246{_}Bound and helpless, he swooned away.
10095-8{_}1247{_}"Brethren," said one of the senior cardinals, "it hath been delivered by the exorcists that a sorcerer or other individual in league with the demon doth usually bear upon his person some visible token of his infernal compact.
10095-8{_}1248{_}I propose that we forthwith institute a search for this stigma, the discovery of which may contribute to justify our proceedings in the eyes of the world."
10095-8{_}1249{_}"I heartily approve of our brother Anno's proposition," said another, "the rather as we cannot possibly fail to discover such a mark, if, indeed, we desire to find it."
10095-8{_}1250{_}The search was accordingly instituted, and had not proceeded far ere a simultaneous yell from all the seven cardinals indicated that their investigation had brought more to light than they had ventured to expect.
10095-8{_}1251{_}The Holy Father had a cloven foot!
10095-8{_}1252{_}For the next five minutes the Cardinals remained utterly stunned, silent, and stupefied with amazement.
10095-8{_}1253{_}As they gradually recovered their faculties it would have become manifest to a nice observer that the Pope had risen very considerably in their good opinion.
10095-8{_}1254{_}"This is an affair requiring very mature deliberation," said one.
10095-8{_}1255{_}"I always feared that we might be proceeding too precipitately," said another.
10095-8{_}1256{_}"It is written, 'the devils believe,'" said a third: "the Holy Father, therefore, is not a heretic at any rate."
10095-8{_}1257{_}"Brethren," said Anno, "this affair, as our brother Benno well remarks, doth indeed call for mature deliberation.
10095-8{_}1258{_}I therefore propose that, instead of smothering his Holiness with cushions, as originally contemplated, we immure him for the present in the dungeon adjoining hereunto, and, after spending the night in meditation and prayer, resume the consideration of the business tomorrow morning."
10095-8{_}1259{_}"Informing the officials of the palace," said Benno, "that his Holiness has retired for his devotions, and desires on no account to be disturbed."
10095-8{_}1260{_}"A pious fraud," said Anno, "which not one of the Fathers would for a moment have scrupled to commit."
10095-8{_}1261{_}The Cardinals accordingly lifted the still insensible Lucifer, and bore him carefully, almost tenderly, to the apartment appointed for his detention.
10095-8{_}1262{_}Each would fain have lingered in hopes of his recovery, but each felt that the eyes of his six brethren were upon him: and all, therefore,  retired simultaneously, each taking a key of the cell.
10095-8{_}1263{_}Lucifer regained consciousness almost immediately afterwards.
10095-8{_}1264{_}He had the most confused idea of the circumstances which had involved him in his present scrape, and could only say to himself that if they were the usual concomitants of the Papal dignity, these were by no means to his taste, and he wished he had been made acquainted with them sooner.
10095-8{_}1265{_}The dungeon was not only perfectly dark, but horribly cold, and the poor devil in his present form had no latent store of infernal heat to draw upon.
10095-8{_}1266{_}His teeth chattered, he shivered in every limb, and felt devoured with hunger and thirst.
10095-8{_}1267{_}There is much probability in the assertion of some of his biographers that it was on this occasion that he invented ardent spirits; but, even if he did, the mere conception of a glass of brandy could only increase his sufferings.
10095-8{_}1268{_}So the long January night wore wearily on, and Lucifer seemed likely to expire from inanition, when a key turned in the lock, and Cardinal Anno cautiously glided in, bearing a lamp, a loaf, half a cold roast kid, and a bottle of wine.
10095-8{_}1269{_}"I trust," he said, bowing courteously, "that I may be excused any slight breach of etiquette of which I may render myself culpable from the difficulty under which I labour of determining whether, under present circumstances, 'Your Holiness,' or 'Your Infernal Majesty' be the form of address most befitting me to employ."
10095-8{_}1270{_}"Bub-ub-bub-boo," went Lucifer, who still had the gag in his mouth.
10095-8{_}1271{_}"Heavens!"
10095-8{_}1272{_}exclaimed the Cardinal, "I crave  your Infernal Holiness's forgiveness.
10095-8{_}1273{_}What a lamentable oversight!"
10095-8{_}1274{_}And, relieving Lucifer from his gag and bonds, he set out the refection, upon which the demon fell voraciously.
10095-8{_}1275{_}"Why the devil, if I may so express myself," pursued Anno, "did not your Holiness inform us that you _were_ the devil?
10095-8{_}1276{_}Not a hand would then have been raised against you.
10095-8{_}1277{_}I have myself been seeking all my life for the audience now happily vouchsafed me.
10095-8{_}1278{_}Whence this mistrust of your faithful Anno, who has served you so loyally and zealously these many years?"
10095-8{_}1279{_}Lucifer pointed significantly to the gag and fetters.
10095-8{_}1280{_}"I shall never forgive myself," protested the Cardinal, "for the part I have borne in this unfortunate transaction.
10095-8{_}1281{_}Next to ministering to your Majesty's bodily necessities, there is nothing I have so much at heart as to express my penitence.
10095-8{_}1282{_}But I entreat your Majesty to remember that I believed myself to be acting in your Majesty's interest by overthrowing a magician who was accustomed to send your Majesty upon errands, and who might at any time enclose you in a box, and cast you into the sea.
10095-8{_}1283{_}It is deplorable that your Majesty's most devoted servants should have been thus misled."
10095-8{_}1284{_}"Reasons of State," suggested Lucifer.
10095-8{_}1285{_}"I trust that they no longer operate," said the Cardinal.
10095-8{_}1286{_}"However, the Sacred College is now fully possessed of the whole matter: it is therefore unnecessary to pursue this department of the subject further.
10095-8{_}1287{_}I would now humbly crave leave to confer with your Majesty, or rather, perhaps, your Holiness, since I am about to speak of spiritual things, on the important and delicate point of your Holiness's successor.
10095-8{_}1288{_}I am ignorant how long your Holiness proposes to occupy the Apostolic chair; but of course you are aware that public opinion will not suffer you to hold it for a term exceeding that of the pontificate of Peter.
10095-8{_}1289{_}A vacancy, therefore, must one day occur; and I am humbly to represent that the office could not be filled by one more congenial than myself to the present incumbent, or on whom he could more fully rely to carry out in every respect his views and intentions."
10095-8{_}1290{_}And the Cardinal proceeded to detail various circumstances of his past life, which certainly seemed to corroborate his assertion.
10095-8{_}1291{_}He had not, however, proceeded far ere he was disturbed by the grating of another key in the lock, and had just time to whisper impressively, "Beware of Benno," ere he dived under a table.
10095-8{_}1292{_}Benno was also provided with a lamp, wine, and cold viands.
10095-8{_}1293{_}Warned by the other lamp and the remains of Lucifer's repast that some colleague had been beforehand with him, and not knowing how many more might be in the field, he came briefly to the point as regarded the Papacy, and preferred his claim in much the same manner as Anno.
