10095-8{_}1924{_}Trojaque nunc stares, Priamique arx alta maneres.
10095-8{_}1925{_}But I can no other.
10095-8{_}1926{_}I am a woman.
10095-8{_}1927{_}May Mantua never entrust her fortunes to the like of me again!
10095-8{_}1928{_}Come with me, I will release thee."
10095-8{_}1929{_}She unlocked his chains; she guided him through the secret passage under the moat; they stood at the exit, in the open air.
10095-8{_}1930{_}"Fly," she said, "and never again draw sword against thy mother.
10095-8{_}1931{_}I will return to my house, and do that to myself which it behoved me to have done ere I released thee."
10095-8{_}1932{_}"Manto," exclaimed Benedetto "a truce to this folly!
10095-8{_}1933{_}Forsake thy dead Duke, and that cheat of Liberty more crazy and fantastic still.
10095-8{_}1934{_}Wed a living Duke in me!"
10095-8{_}1935{_}"Never!"
10095-8{_}1936{_}exclaimed Manto.
10095-8{_}1937{_}"I love thee more than any man living on earth, and I would not espouse thee if the earth held no other."
10095-8{_}1938{_}"Thou canst not help thyself," he rejoined; "thou hast revealed to me the secret of this passage.
10095-8{_}1939{_}I hasten to the camp.
10095-8{_}1940{_}I return in an hour with an army, and wilt thou, wilt thou not,  to-morrow's sun shall behold thee the partner of my throne!"
10095-8{_}1941{_}Manto wore a poniard.
10095-8{_}1942{_}She struck Benedetto to the heart, and he fell dead.
10095-8{_}1943{_}She drew the corpse back into the passage, and hurried to her home.
10095-8{_}1944{_}Opening her master's volume again, she read:    Tædet coeli convexa tueri.
10095-8{_}1945{_}A few minutes afterwards her father entered the chamber to tell her he had at last found the philosopher's stone, but, perceiving his daughter hanging by her girdle, he forbore to intrude upon her, and returned to his laboratory.
10095-8{_}1946{_}It was time.
10095-8{_}1947{_}A sentinel of the besiegers had marked Benedetto's fall, and the disappearance of the body into the earth.
10095-8{_}1948{_}A pool of blood revealed the entrance to the passage.
10095-8{_}1949{_}Ere sunrise Mantua was full of Frederick's soldiers, full also of burning houses, rifled sanctuaries, violated damsels, children playing with their dead mothers' breasts, especially full of citizens protesting that they had ever longed for the restoration of the Emperor, and that this was the happiest day of their lives.
10095-8{_}1950{_}Frederick waited till everybody was killed, then entered the city and proclaimed an amnesty.
10095-8{_}1951{_}Virgil's bust was broken, and his writings burned with Manto's body.
10095-8{_}1952{_}The flames glowed on the dead face, which gleamed as it were with pleasure.
10095-8{_}1953{_}The old alchemist had been slain among his crucibles; his scrolls were preserved with jealous care.
10095-8{_}1954{_}But Manto found another father.
10095-8{_}1955{_}She sat at Virgil's feet in Elysium; and as he stroked the fair head, now golden with perpetual youth,  listened to his mild reproofs and his cheerful oracles.
10095-8{_}1956{_}By her side stood a bowl filled with the untasted waters of Lethe.
10095-8{_}1957{_}"Woe," said Virgil--but his manner contradicted his speech--"woe to the idealist and enthusiast!
10095-8{_}1958{_}Woe to them who live in the world to come!
10095-8{_}1959{_}Woe to them who live only for a hope whose fulfilment they will not behold on earth!
10095-8{_}1960{_}Drink not, therefore, of that cup, dear child, lest Duke Virgil's day should come, and thou shouldst not know it.
10095-8{_}1961{_}For come it will, and all the sooner for thy tragedy and thy comedy."
10095-8{_}1962{_}THE CLAW   The balm and stillness of a summer's night enveloped a spacious piazza in the city of Shylock and Desdemona.
10095-8{_}1963{_}The sky teemed with light drifting clouds through which the beaming of the full moon broke at intervals upon some lamp-lit palace, thronged and musical, for it was a night of festivity, or silvered the dull creeping waters.
10095-8{_}1964{_}Ever and anon some richly attired young patrician descended the steps of one or other of these mansions, and hurried across the wide area to the canal stairs, where his gondola awaited him.
10095-8{_}1965{_}Whoever did this could not but observe a tall female figure, which, cloaked and masked, walked backwards and forwards across the piazza, regarding no one, yet with an air that seemed to invite a companion.
10095-8{_}1966{_}More than one of the young nobles approached the presumably fair peripatetic, and, with courtesy commonly in inverse ratio to the amount of wine he was carrying home, proffered his escort to his gondola.
10095-8{_}1967{_}Whenever this happened the figure removed her mask and unclasped her robe, and revealed a sight which for one moment rooted the young man to the earth and in the next sent him scampering to his bark.
10095-8{_}1968{_}For the countenance was a death's head, and the breast was that of a mouldering skeleton.
10095-8{_}1969{_}At last, however, a youth presented himself who, more courageous or more tipsy than his fellows, or more helplessly paralysed with horror than they, did not decline the proffered caress, and suffered himself to be drawn within the goblin's accursed embrace.
10095-8{_}1970{_}Valiant or pot-valiant, great was his relief at finding himself clasped, instead of by a loathsome spectre, by a silver-haired man of noble presence, yet with a countenance indescribably haggard and anxious.
10095-8{_}1971{_}"Come, my son," he cried, "hasten whither the rewards of thy intrepidity await thee.
10095-8{_}1972{_}Impouch the purse of Fortunatus!
10095-8{_}1973{_}Indue the signet of Solomon!"
10095-8{_}1974{_}The young man hesitated.
10095-8{_}1975{_}"Is there nought else?"
10095-8{_}1976{_}he cautiously demanded.
10095-8{_}1977{_}"Needs it not that I should renounce my baptism?
10095-8{_}1978{_}Must I not subscribe an infernal compact?"
10095-8{_}1979{_}"In thy own blood, my son," cheerfully responded the old gentleman.
10095-8{_}1980{_}"Peradventure," hesitatingly interrogated the youth, "peradventure you are _he_?"
10095-8{_}1981{_}"Not so, my son, upon honour," returned the mysterious personage.
10095-8{_}1982{_}"I am but a distressed magician, at this present in fearful straits, from which I look to be delivered by thee."
10095-8{_}1983{_}The youth gazed some moments at his companion's head, and then still more earnestly at his feet.
10095-8{_}1984{_}He then yielded his own hand to him, and the pair crossed the piazza, almost at a run, the magician ever ejaculating, "Speed!
10095-8{_}1985{_}speed!"
10095-8{_}1986{_}They paused at the foot of a lofty tower, doorless and windowless, with no visible access of any kind.
10095-8{_}1987{_}But the magician signed with his hand, pronounced some cabalistical words, and instantly  stone and lime fell asunder and revealed an entrance through which they passed, and which immediately closed behind them.
10095-8{_}1988{_}The youth quaked at finding himself alone in utter darkness with he knew not what, but the wizard whistled, and a severed hand appeared in air bearing a lamp which illuminated a long winding staircase.
10095-8{_}1989{_}The old man motioned to the youth to precede him, nor dared he refuse, though feeling as though he would have given the world for the very smallest relic of the very smallest saint.
10095-8{_}1990{_}The distorted shadows of the twain, dancing on stair and wall with the wavering lamp-shine, seemed phantoms capering in an infernal revel, and he glanced back ever and anon weening to see himself dogged by some frightful monster, but he saw only the silver hair and sable velvet of the dignified old man.
10095-8{_}1991{_}After the ascent of many steps a door opened before them, and they found themselves in a spacious chamber, brightly, yet from its size imperfectly illumined by a single large lamp.
10095-8{_}1992{_}It was wainscoted with ebony, and the furniture was of the same.
10095-8{_}1993{_}A long table was covered with scrolls, skulls, crucibles, crystals, star-charts, geomantic figures, and other appurtenances of a magician's calling.
10095-8{_}1994{_}Tomes of necromantic lore lined the walls, which were yet principally occupied with crystal vessels, in which foul beings seemed dimly and confusedly to agitate themselves.
10095-8{_}1995{_}The magician signed to his visitor to be seated, sat down himself and began:  "Brave youth, ere entering upon the boundless power and riches that await thee, learn who I am and why I have brought thee here.
10095-8{_}1996{_}Behold in me  no vulgar wizard, no mere astrologer or alchemist, but a compeer of Merlin and Michael Scott, with whose name it may be the nurse of thy infancy hath oft-times quelled thy froward humours.
10095-8{_}1997{_}I am Peter of Abano, falsely believed to have lain two centuries buried in the semblance of a dog under a heap of stones hurled by the furious populace, but in truth walking earth to this day, in virtue of the compact now to be revealed to thee.
10095-8{_}1998{_}Hearken, my son!
10095-8{_}1999{_}Vain must be the machinations of my enemies, vain the onslaughts of the rabble, so long as I fulfil a certain contract registered in hell's chancery, as I have now done these three hundred years.
10095-8{_}2000{_}And the condition is this, that every year I present unto the Demon one who hath at my persuasion assigned his soul to him in exchange for power, riches, knowledge, magical gifts, or whatever else his heart chiefly desireth; nor until this present year have I perilled the fulfilment of my obligation.
10095-8{_}2001{_}Seest thou these scrolls?
10095-8{_}2002{_}They are the assignments of which I have spoken.
10095-8{_}2003{_}It would amaze thee to scan the subscriptions, and perceive in these the signatures of men exemplary in the eyes of their fellows, clothed with high dignities in Church and State--nay sometimes redolent of the very odour of sanctity.
10095-8{_}2004{_}Never hath my sagacity deceived me until this year, when, smitten with the fair promise of a youth of singular impishness, I omitted to take due note of his consumptive habit, and have but this afternoon encountered his funeral.
10095-8{_}2005{_}This is the last day of my year, and should my engagement be unredeemed when the sun attains the cusp of that nethermost house of heaven which he is even now traversing, I must  become an inmate of the infernal kingdom.
10095-8{_}2006{_}No time has remained for nice investigation.
10095-8{_}2007{_}I have therefore proved the courage of the Venetian youth in the manner thou knowest, and thou alone hast sustained the ordeal.
10095-8{_}2008{_}Fail not at my bidding, or thou quittest not this chamber alive.
10095-8{_}2009{_}For when the Demon comes to bear me away, he will assuredly rend thee in pieces for being found in my company.
10095-8{_}2010{_}Thou hast, therefore, everything to gain and nothing to lose by joining the goodly fellowship of my mates and partners.
10095-8{_}2011{_}Delay not, time urges, night deepens, they that would drink thy blood are abroad.
10095-8{_}2012{_}Hearest thou not the moaning and pelting of the rising storm, and the muttering and scraping of my imprisoned goblins?
10095-8{_}2013{_}Save us, I entreat, I command, save us both!"
10095-8{_}2014{_}Screaming with agitation the aged sorcerer laid a scroll engrossed with fairly written characters before the youth, stabbed the latter's arm with a stylus that at once evoked and collected the crimson stream, thrust this into his hand and strove to guide it to the parchment, chanting at the same time litanies to the infernal powers.
10095-8{_}2015{_}The crystal flagons rang like one great harmonica with shrill but spirit-stirring music; volumes of vaporous perfumes diffused themselves through the apartment, and an endless procession of treasure-laden figures defiled before the bewildered youth.
10095-8{_}2016{_}He seemed buried in the opulence of the world, as he sat up to his waist in gold and jewels; all the earth's beauty gazed at him through eyes brilliant and countless as the stars of heaven; courtiers beckoned him to thrones; battle-steeds neighed and pawed for his mounting; laden tables allured every appetite; vassals bent in  homage; slaves fell prostrate at his feet.
10095-8{_}2017{_}Now he seemed to collect or disperse legions of spirits with the waving of a wand; anon, as he pronounced a spell, golden dragons glided away from boughs laden with golden fruits.
10095-8{_}2018{_}Well for him, doubtless, that in him Nature had kneaded from ordinary clay as unimaginative a youth as could be found in Venice: yet even so, dazzled with glamour, intoxicated with illusion, less and less able to resist the cunningly mingled caresses, entreaties, and menaces of Abano, he could not refrain from tracing a few characters with the stylus, when, catching reflected in a mirror the old magician's expression of wolfish glee, he dropped the instrument from his grasp, and cast his eye upwards as if appealing to Heaven.
10095-8{_}2019{_}But every drop of blood seemed frozen in his frame as he beheld an enormous claw thrust through the roof, member as it seemed of some being too gigantic to be contained in the chamber or the tower itself.
10095-8{_}2020{_}Cold, poignant, glittering as steel, it rested upon a socket of the repulsive hue of jaundiced ivory, with no vestige of a foot or anything to relieve its naked horror as, rigid and lifeless, yet plainly with a mighty force behind it, it pointed at the magician's heart.
10095-8{_}2021{_}As Abano, following the youth's eye, caught sight of the portent, his visage assumed an expression of frantic horror, his spells died upon his lips, and the gorgeous figures became grinning apes or blotchy toads: madly he seized the young man's hand, and strove to force him to complete his signature.
10095-8{_}2022{_}The robust youth felt as an infant in his grasp, but ere the stylus could be again thrust upon him the first stroke of the midnight hour  rang through the chamber, and instantly the gigantic talon pierced Abano from breast to back, projecting far beyond his shoulders, and swept him upwards to the roof, through which both disappeared without leaving a trace of their passage.
10095-8{_}2023{_}Horror and thankfulness rushed together into the young man's mind, and there contended for some brief instants: but as the last stroke sounded all the crystal vials shivered with a stunning crash, and their hellish inmates, rejoicing in their deliverance, swarmed into the chamber.
10095-8{_}2024{_}All made for the youth, who, tugged, clawed, fondled, bitten, beslimed, blinded, deafened, beset in every way by creatures of indescribable loathsomeness, grasped frantically as his sole weapon, the stylus; but it had become a writhing serpent.
10095-8{_}2025{_}This was too much, sense forsook him on the spot.
10095-8{_}2026{_}On recovering consciousness he found himself stretched on a pallet in the dungeons of the Inquisition.
10095-8{_}2027{_}The Inquisitors sat on their tribunals; black-robed familiars flitted about, or waited attentive upon their orders; one expert in ecclesiastical jurisprudence proved the edge of an axe, and another heated pincers in a chafing-dish; dismal groans pierced the massy walls; two sturdy fellows, stripped to the waist, adjusted the rollers of a rack.
10095-8{_}2028{_}A surgeon approached the bedside, bearing a phial and a lancet.
10095-8{_}2029{_}The youth screamed and again became insensible.
10095-8{_}2030{_}But his affright was groundless.
10095-8{_}2031{_}The Inquisitors had already taken cognisance of Abano's scrolls, and found that, touching these at least, he had spoken sooth.
10095-8{_}2032{_}Besides kings, princes, ministers, magistrates, and other secular persons who had owed their success in life to dealings with the devil under his mediation, the infernal bondsmen included so many pillars of the Church and champions of the Faith; prelates plenty, abbots in abundance, cardinals not a few, a (some whispered _the_) Pope; above all, so many of the Inquisitors themselves, that further inquiry could evidently nowise conduce to edification.
10095-8{_}2033{_}The surgeon, therefore, infused an opiate into the veins of the unconscious youth, and he came to himself upon a galley speeding him to the holy war in Cyprus, where he fell fighting the Turk.
10095-8{_}2034{_}ALEXANDER THE RATCATCHER   "Alexander Octavus mures, qui Urbem supra modum vexabant, anathemate perculit."[--_Palatius.
10095-8{_}2035{_}Fasti Cardinalium_, tom.
10095-8{_}2036{_}v.p.
10095-8{_}2037{_}46.]
10095-8{_}2038{_}I   "Rome and her rats are at the point of battle!"
10095-8{_}2039{_}This metaphor of Menenius Agrippa's became, history records, matter of fact in 1689, when rats pervaded the Eternal City from garret to cellar, and Pope Alexander the Eighth seriously apprehended the fate of Bishop Hatto.
10095-8{_}2040{_}The situation worried him sorely; he had but lately attained the tiara at an advanced age--the twenty-fourth hour, as he himself remarked in extenuation of his haste to enrich his nephews.
10095-8{_}2041{_}The time vouchsafed for worthier deeds was brief, and he dreaded descending to posterity as the Rat Pope.
10095-8{_}2042{_}Witty and genial, his sense of humour teased him with a full perception of the absurdity of his position.
10095-8{_}2043{_}Peter and Pasquin concurred in forbidding him to desert his post; and he derived but small comfort from the ingenuity of his flatterers, who compared him to St. Paul contending with beasts at Ephesus.
10095-8{_}2044{_}It wanted three half-hours to midnight, as Alexander sat amid traps and ratsbane in his  chamber in the Vatican, under the protection of two enormous cats and a British terrier.
10095-8{_}2045{_}A silver bell stood ready to his hand, should the aid of the attendant chamberlains be requisite.
10095-8{_}2046{_}The walls had been divested of their tapestries, and the floor gleamed with pounded glass.
10095-8{_}2047{_}A tome of legendary lore lay open at the history of the Piper of Hamelin.
10095-8{_}2048{_}All was silence, save for the sniffing and scratching of the dog and a sound of subterranean scraping and gnawing.
10095-8{_}2049{_}"Why tarries Cardinal Barbadico thus?"
10095-8{_}2050{_}the Pope at last asked himself aloud.
10095-8{_}2051{_}The inquiry was answered by a wild burst of squeaking and clattering and scurrying to and fro, as who should say, "We've eaten him!
10095-8{_}2052{_}We've eaten him!"
10095-8{_}2053{_}But this exultation was at least premature, for just as the terrified Pope clutched his bell, the door opened to the narrowest extent compatible with the admission of an ecclesiastical personage of dignified presence, and Cardinal Barbadico hastily squeezed himself through.
10095-8{_}2054{_}"I shall hardly trust myself upon these stairs again," he remarked, "unless under the escort of your Holiness's terrier."
10095-8{_}2055{_}"Take him, my son, and a cruse of holy water to boot," the Pope responded.
10095-8{_}2056{_}"Now, how go things in the city?"
10095-8{_}2057{_}"As ill as may be, your Holiness.
10095-8{_}2058{_}Not a saint stirs a finger to help us.
10095-8{_}2059{_}The country-folk shun the city, the citizens seek the country.
10095-8{_}2060{_}The multitude of enemies increases hour by hour.
10095-8{_}2061{_}They set at defiance the anathemas fulminated by your Holiness, the spiritual censures placarded in the churches, and the citation to appear before the ecclesiastical courts, although assured that  their cause shall be pleaded by the ablest advocates in Rome.
10095-8{_}2062{_}The cats, amphibious with alarm, are taking to the Tiber.
10095-8{_}2063{_}Vainly the city reeks with toasted cheese, and the Commissary-General reports himself short of arsenic."
10095-8{_}2064{_}"And how are the people taking it?"
10095-8{_}2065{_}demanded Alexander.
10095-8{_}2066{_}"To what cause do they attribute the public calamity?"
10095-8{_}2067{_}"Generally speaking, to the sins of your Holiness," replied the Cardinal.
10095-8{_}2068{_}"Cardinal!"
10095-8{_}2069{_}exclaimed Alexander indignantly.
10095-8{_}2070{_}"I crave pardon for my temerity," returned Barbadico.
10095-8{_}2071{_}"It is with difficulty that I force myself to speak, but I am bound to lay the ungrateful truth before your Holiness.
10095-8{_}2072{_}The late Pope, as all men know, was a personage of singular sanctity."
10095-8{_}2073{_}"Far too upright for this fallen world," observed Alexander with unction.
10095-8{_}2074{_}"I will not dispute," responded the Cardinal, "that the head of Innocent the Eleventh might have been more fitly graced by a halo than by a tiara.
10095-8{_}2075{_}But the vulgar are incapable of placing themselves at this point of view.
10095-8{_}2076{_}They know that the rats hardly squeaked under Innocent, and that they swarm under Alexander.
10095-8{_}2077{_}What wonder if they suspect your Holiness of familiarity with Beelzebub, the patron of vermin, and earnestly desire that he would take you to himself?
10095-8{_}2078{_}Vainly have I represented to them the unreasonableness of imposing upon him a trouble he may well deem superfluous, considering your Holiness's infirm health and advanced age.
10095-8{_}2079{_}Vainly, too, have I pointed out that your anathema has actually produced all the effect that  could have been reasonably anticipated from any similar manifesto on your predecessor's part.
10095-8{_}2080{_}They won't see it.
10095-8{_}2081{_}And, in fact, might I humbly advise, it does appear impolitic to hurl anathemas unless your Holiness knows that some one will be hit.
10095-8{_}2082{_}It might be opportune, for example, to excommunicate Father Molinos, now fast in the dungeons of St. Angelo, unless, indeed, the rats have devoured him there.
10095-8{_}2083{_}But I question the expediency of going much further."
10095-8{_}2084{_}"Cardinal," said the Pope, "you think yourself prodigiously clever, but you ought to know that the state of public opinion allowed us no alternative.
10095-8{_}2085{_}Moreover, I will give you a wrinkle, in case you should ever come to be Pope yourself.
10095-8{_}2086{_}It is unwise to allow ancient prerogatives to fall entirely into desuetude.
10095-8{_}2087{_}Far-seeing men prognosticate a great revival of sacerdotalism in the nineteenth century, and what is impotent in an age of sense may be formidable in an age of nonsense.
10095-8{_}2088{_}Further, we know not from one day to another whether we may not be absolutely necessitated to excommunicate that fautor of Gallicanism, Louis the Fourteenth, and before launching our bolt at a king, we may think well to test its efficacy upon a rat.
10095-8{_}2089{_}_Fiat experimentum._ And now to return to our rats, from which we have ratted.
10095-8{_}2090{_}Is there indeed no hope?"
10095-8{_}2091{_}"_Lateat scintillula forsan_," said the Cardinal mysteriously.
10095-8{_}2092{_}"Ha!
10095-8{_}2093{_}How so?"
10095-8{_}2094{_}eagerly demanded Alexander.
10095-8{_}2095{_}"Our hopes," answered the Cardinal, "are associated with the recent advent to this city of an extraordinary personage."
10095-8{_}2096{_}"Explain," urged the Pope.
10095-8{_}2097{_}"I speak," resumed the Cardinal, "of an aged man of no plebeian mien or bearing, albeit most shabbily attired in the skins, now fabulously cheap, of the vermin that torment us; who, professing to practise as an herbalist, some little time ago established himself in an obscure street of no good repute.
10095-8{_}2098{_}A tortoise hangs in his needy shop, nor are stuffed alligators lacking.
10095-8{_}2099{_}Understanding that he was resorted to by such as have need of philters and love-potions, or are incommoded by the longevity of parents and uncles, I was about to have him arrested, when I received a report which gave me pause.
10095-8{_}2100{_}This concerned the singular intimacy which appeared to subsist between him and our enemies.
10095-8{_}2101{_}When he left home, it was averred, he was attended by troops of them obedient to his beck and call, and spies had observed him banqueting them at his counter, the rats sitting erect and comporting themselves with perfect decorum.
10095-8{_}2102{_}I resolved to investigate the matter for myself.
10095-8{_}2103{_}Looking into his house through an unshuttered window, I perceived him in truth surrounded by feasting and gambolling rats; but when the door was opened in obedience to my attendants' summons, he appeared to be entirely alone.
10095-8{_}2104{_}Laying down a pestle and mortar, he greeted me by name with an easy familiarity which for the moment quite disconcerted me, and inquired what had procured him the honour of my visit.
10095-8{_}2105{_}Recovering myself, and wishing to intimidate him:  "'I desire in the first place,' I said, 'to point out to you your grave transgression of municipal regulations in omitting to paint your name over your shop.'
10095-8{_}2106{_}"'Call me Rattila,' he rejoined with unconcern, 'and state your further business.'
10095-8{_}2107{_}"I felt myself on the wrong tack, and hastened to interrogate him respecting his relations with our adversaries.
10095-8{_}2108{_}He frankly admitted his acquaintance with rattery in all its branches, and his ability to deliver the city from this scourge, but his attitude towards your Holiness was so deficient in respect that I question whether I ought to report it."
10095-8{_}2109{_}"Proceed, son," said the Pope; "we will not be deterred from providing for the public weal by the ribaldry of a ratcatcher."
10095-8{_}2110{_}"He scoffed at what he termed your Holiness's absurd position, and affirmed that the world had seldom beheld, or would soon behold again, so ridiculous a spectacle as a Pope besieged by rats.
10095-8{_}2111{_}'I can help your master,' he continued, 'and am willing; but my honour, like his, is aspersed in the eyes of the multitude, and he must come to my aid, if I am to come to his.'
10095-8{_}2112{_}"I prayed him to be more explicit, and offered to be the bearer of any communication to your Holiness.
10095-8{_}2113{_}"'I will unfold myself to no one but the Pope himself,' he replied, 'and the interview must take place when and where I please to appoint.
10095-8{_}2114{_}Let him meet me this very midnight, and alone, in the fifth chamber of the Appartamento Borgia.'
10095-8{_}2115{_}"'The Appartamento Borgia!'
10095-8{_}2116{_}I exclaimed in consternation.
10095-8{_}2117{_}'The saloons which the wicked Pope Alexander the Sixth nocturnally perambulates, mingling poisons that have long lost their potency for Cardinals who have long lost their lives!'
10095-8{_}2118{_}"'Have a care!'
10095-8{_}2119{_}he exclaimed sharply.
10095-8{_}2120{_}'You speak to his late Holiness's most intimate friend.'
10095-8{_}2121{_}"'Then,' I answered, 'you must obviously be the Devil, and I am not at present empowered to negotiate with your Infernal Majesty.
10095-8{_}2122{_}Consider, however, the peril and inconvenience of visiting at dead of night rooms closed for generations.
10095-8{_}2123{_}Think of the chills and cobwebs.
10095-8{_}2124{_}Weigh the probability of his Holiness being devoured by rats.'
10095-8{_}2125{_}"'I guarantee his Holiness absolute immunity from cold,' he replied, 'and that none of my subjects shall molest him either going or returning.'
10095-8{_}2126{_}"'But,' I objected, 'granting that you are not the Devil, how the devil, let me ask, do you expect to gain admittance at midnight to the Appartamento Borgia?'
10095-8{_}2127{_}"'Think you I cannot pass through a stone wall?'
10095-8{_}2128{_}answered he, and vanished in an instant.
10095-8{_}2129{_}A tremendous scampering of rats immediately ensued, then all was silence.
10095-8{_}2130{_}"On recovering in some measure from my astounded condition, I caused strict search to be made throughout the shop.
10095-8{_}2131{_}Nothing came to light but herbalists' stuff and ordinary medicines.
10095-8{_}2132{_}And now, Holy Father, your Holiness's resolution?
10095-8{_}2133{_}Reflect well.
10095-8{_}2134{_}This Rattila may be the King of the Rats, or he may be Beelzebub in person."
10095-8{_}2135{_}Alexander the Eighth was principally considered by his contemporaries in the light of a venerable fox, but the lion had by no means been omitted from his composition.
10095-8{_}2136{_}"All powers of good forbid," he exclaimed, "that a Pope and a Prince should shrink from  peril which the safety of the State summons him to encounter!
10095-8{_}2137{_}I will confront this wizard, this goblin, in the place of his own appointing, under his late intimate friend's very nose.
10095-8{_}2138{_}I am a man of many transgressions, but something assures me that Heaven will not deem this a fit occasion for calling them to remembrance.
10095-8{_}2139{_}Time presses; I lead on; follow, Cardinal Barbadico, follow!
10095-8{_}2140{_}Yet stay, let us not forget temporal and spiritual armouries."
10095-8{_}2141{_}And hastily providing himself with a lamp, a petronel, a bunch of keys, a crucifix, a vial of holy water, and a manual of exorcisms, the Pope passed through a secret door in a corner of his chamber, followed by the Cardinal bearing another lamp and a naked sword, and preceded by the dog and the two cats, all ardent and undaunted as champions bound to the Holy Land for the recovery of the Holy Sepulchre.
10095-8{_}2142{_}II   The wizard had kept his word.
10095-8{_}2143{_}Not a rat was seen or heard upon the pilgrimage, which was exceedingly toilsome to the aged Pope, from the number of passages to be threaded and doors to be unlocked.
10095-8{_}2144{_}At length the companions stood before the portal of the Appartamento Borgia.
10095-8{_}2145{_}"Your Holiness must enter alone," Cardinal Barbadico admonished, with manifest reluctance.
10095-8{_}2146{_}"Await my return," enjoined the Pontiff, in a tone of more confidence than he could actually feel, as, after much grinding and grating, the  massive door swung heavily back, and he passed on into the dim, unexplored space beyond.
10095-8{_}2147{_}The outer air, streaming in as though eager to indemnify itself for years of exile, smote and swayed the flame of the Pope's lamp, whose feeble ray flitted from floor to ceiling as the decrepit man, weary with the way he had traversed and the load he was bearing, tottered and stumbled painfully along, ever and anon arrested by a closed door, which he unlocked with prodigious difficulty.
10095-8{_}2148{_}The cats cowered close to the Cardinal; the dog at first accompanied the Pope, but whined so grievously, as though he beheld a spirit, that Alexander bade him back.
10095-8{_}2149{_}Supreme is the spell of the _genius loci_.
10095-8{_}2150{_}The chambers traversed by the Pope were in fact adorned with fair examples of the painter's art, mostly scriptural in subject, but some inspired with the devout Pantheism in which all creeds are reconciled.
10095-8{_}2151{_}All were alike invisible to the Pontiff, who, with the dim flicker of his lamp, could no more discern Judaea wed with Egypt on the frescoed ceiling than, with the human limitation of his faculties, he could foresee that the ill-reputed rooms would one day harbour a portion of the Vatican Library, so greatly enriched by himself.
10095-8{_}2152{_}Nothing but sinister memories and vague alarms presented themselves to his imagination.
10095-8{_}2153{_}The atmosphere, heavy and brooding from the long exclusion of the outer air, seemed to weigh upon him with the density of matter, and to afford the stuff out of which phantasmal bodies perpetually took shape and, as he half persuaded himself, substance.
10095-8{_}2154{_}Creeping and tottering between bowl and cord, shielding himself with  lamp and crucifix from Michelotto's spectral poniard and more fearful contact with fleshless Vanozzas and mouldering Giulias, the Pope urged, or seemed to urge, his course amid phantom princes and cardinals, priests and courtesans, soldiers and serving-men, dancers, drinkers, dicers, Bacchic and Cotyttian workers of whatsoever least beseemed the inmates of a Pontifical household, until, arrived in the fifth chamber, close by the, to him, invisible picture of the Resurrection, he sank exhausted into a spacious chair that seemed placed for his reception, and for a moment closed his eyes.
10095-8{_}2155{_}Opening them immediately afterwards, he saw with relief that the phantoms had vanished, and that he confronted what at least seemed a fellow-mortal, in the ancient ratcatcher, habited precisely as Cardinal Barbadico had described, yet, for all his mean apparel, wearing the air of one wont to confer with the potentates of the earth on other subjects than the extermination of rats.
10095-8{_}2156{_}"This is noble of your Holiness--really," he said, bowing with mock reverence.
10095-8{_}2157{_}"A second Leo the Great!"
10095-8{_}2158{_}"I tell you what, my man," responded Alexander, feeling it very necessary to assert his dignity while any of it remained, "you are not to imagine that, because I have humoured you so far as to grant you an audience at an unusual place and time, I am going to stand any amount of your nonsense and impertinence.
10095-8{_}2159{_}You can catch our rats, can you?
10095-8{_}2160{_}Catch them then, and you need not fear that we shall treat you like the Pied Piper of Hamelin.
10095-8{_}2161{_}You have committed sundry rascalities, no doubt?
10095-8{_}2162{_}A pardon shall  be made out for you.
10095-8{_}2163{_}You want a patent or a privilege for your ratsbane?
10095-8{_}2164{_}You shall have it.
10095-8{_}2165{_}So to work, in the name of St. Muscipulus!
10095-8{_}2166{_}and you may keep the tails and skins."
10095-8{_}2167{_}"Alexander," said the ratcatcher composedly, "I would not commend or dispraise you unduly, but this I may say, that of all the Popes I have known you are the most exuberant in hypocrisy and the most deficient in penetration.
10095-8{_}2168{_}The most hypocritical, because you well know, and know that I know that you know, that you are not conversing with an ordinary ratcatcher: had you deemed me such, you would never have condescended to meet me at this hour and place.
10095-8{_}2169{_}The least penetrating, because you apparently have not yet discovered to whom you are speaking.
10095-8{_}2170{_}Do you really mean to say that you do not know me?"
10095-8{_}2171{_}"I believe I have seen your face before," said Alexander, "and all the more likely as I was inspector of prisons when I was Cardinal."
10095-8{_}2172{_}"Then look yonder," enjoined the ratcatcher, as he pointed to the frescoed wall, at the same time vehemently snapping his fingers.
10095-8{_}2173{_}Phosphoric sparks hissed and crackled forth, and coalesced into a blue lambent flame, which concentrated itself upon a depicted figure, whose precise attitude the ratcatcher assumed as he dropped upon his knees.
10095-8{_}2174{_}The Pope shrieked with amazement, for, although the splendid Pontifical vestments had become ragged fur, in every other respect the kneeling figure was the counterpart of the painted one, and the painted one was Pinturicchio's portrait of Pope Alexander the Sixth kneeling as a witness of the Resurrection.
10095-8{_}2175{_}Alexander the Eighth would fain have imitated  his predecessor's attitude, but terror bound him to his chair, and the adjuration of his patron St. Mark which struggled towards his lips never arrived there.
10095-8{_}2176{_}The book of exorcisms fell from his paralysed hand, and the vial of holy water lay in shivers upon the floor.
10095-8{_}2177{_}Ere he could collect himself, the dead Pope had seated himself beside the Pope with one foot in the grave, and, fondling a ferret-skin, proceeded to enter into conversation.
10095-8{_}2178{_}"What fear you?"
10095-8{_}2179{_}he asked.
10095-8{_}2180{_}"Why should I harm you?
10095-8{_}2181{_}None can say that I ever injured any one for any cause but my own advantage, and to injure your Holiness now would be to obstruct a design which I have particularly at heart."
10095-8{_}2182{_}"I crave your Holiness's forgiveness," rejoined the Eighth Alexander, "but you must be aware that you left the world with a reputation which disqualifies you for the society of any Pope in the least careful of his character.
10095-8{_}2183{_}It positively compromises me to have so much as the ghost of a person so universally decried as your Holiness under my roof, and you would infinitely oblige me by forthwith repairing to your own place, which I take to be about four thousand miles below where you are sitting.
10095-8{_}2184{_}I could materially facilitate and accelerate your Holiness's transit thither if you would be so kind as to hand me that little book of exorcisms."
10095-8{_}2185{_}"How is the fine gold become dim!"
10095-8{_}2186{_}exclaimed Alexander the Sixth.
10095-8{_}2187{_}"Popes in bondage to moralists!
10095-8{_}2188{_}Popes nervous about public opinion!
10095-8{_}2189{_}Is there another judge of morals than the Pope speaking _ex cathedra_, as I always did?
10095-8{_}2190{_}Is the Church to frame herself after the prescriptions  of heathen philosophers and profane jurists?
10095-8{_}2191{_}How, then, shall she be terrible as an army with banners?
10095-8{_}2192{_}Did I concern myself with such pedantry when the Kings of Spain and Portugal came to me like cats suing for morsels, and I gave them the West and the East?"
10095-8{_}2193{_}"It is true," Alexander the Eighth allowed, "that the lustre of the Church hath of late been obfuscated by the prevalence of heresy."
10095-8{_}2194{_}"It isn't the heretics," Borgia insisted.
10095-8{_}2195{_}"It is the degeneracy of the Popes.
10095-8{_}2196{_}A shabby lot!
10095-8{_}2197{_}You, Alexander, are about the best of them; but the least Cardinal about my Court would have thought himself bigger than you."
10095-8{_}2198{_}Alexander's spirit rose.
10095-8{_}2199{_}"I would suggest," he said, "that this haughty style is little in keeping with the sordid garb wherein your Holiness, consistent after death as in your life, masquerades to the scandal and distress of the faithful."
10095-8{_}2200{_}"How can I other?
10095-8{_}2201{_}Has your Holiness forgotten your Rabelais?"
10095-8{_}2202{_}"The works of that eminent Doctor and Divine," answered Alexander the Eighth, "are seldom long absent from my hands, yet I fail to remember in what manner they elucidate the present topic."
10095-8{_}2203{_}"Let me refresh your memory," rejoined Borgia, and, producing a volume of the Sage of Meudon, he turned to the chapter descriptive of the employments of various eminent inhabitants of the nether world, and pointed to the sentence:  "LE PAPE ALEXANDRE ESTOYT PRENEUR DE RATZ."
10095-8{_}2204{_}[*]  [Footnote: _Pantagruel_, Book XI.
10095-8{_}2205{_}ch.
10095-8{_}2206{_}30.]
10095-8{_}2207{_}"Is this indeed sooth?"
10095-8{_}2208{_}demanded his successor.
10095-8{_}2209{_}"How else should François Rabelais have affirmed it?"
10095-8{_}2210{_}responded Borgia.
10095-8{_}2211{_}"When I arrived in the subterranean kingdom, I found it in the same condition as your Holiness's dominions at the present moment, eaten up by rats.
10095-8{_}2212{_}The attention which, during my earthly pilgrimage, I had devoted to the science of toxicology indicated me as a person qualified to abate the nuisance, which commission I executed with such success, that I received the appointment of Ratcatcher to his Infernal Majesty, and so discharged its duties as to merit a continuance of the good opinion which had always been entertained of me in that exalted quarter.
10095-8{_}2213{_}After a while, however, interest began to be made for me in even more elevated spheres.
10095-8{_}2214{_}I had not been able to cram Heaven with Spaniards, as I had crammed the Sacred College--on the contrary.
10095-8{_}2215{_}Truth to speak, my nation has not largely contributed to the population of the regions above.
10095-8{_}2216{_}But some of us are people of consequence.
10095-8{_}2217{_}My great-grandson, the General of the Jesuits, who, as such, had the ear of St. Ignatius Loyola, represented that had I adhered strictly to my vows, he could never have come into existence, and that the Society would thus have wanted one of its brightest ornaments.
10095-8{_}2218{_}This argument naturally had great weight with St. Ignatius, the rather as he, too, was my countryman.
10095-8{_}2219{_}Much also was said of the charity I had shown to the exiled Jews, which St. Dominic was pleased to say made him feel ashamed of himself when he came to think of it; for my having fed my people in time of dearth, instead of contriving famines to enrich myself, as so many Popes' nephews have done since; and  of the splendid order in which I kept the College of Cardinals.
10095-8{_}2220{_}Columbus said a good word for me, and Savonarola did not oppose.
10095-8{_}2221{_}Finally I was allowed to come upstairs, and exercise my profession on earth.
10095-8{_}2222{_}But mark what pitfalls line the good man's path!
10095-8{_}2223{_}I never could resist tampering with drugs of a deleterious nature, and was constantly betrayed by the thirst for scientific experiment into practices incompatible with the public health.
10095-8{_}2224{_}The good nature which my detractors have not denied me was a veritable snare.
10095-8{_}2225{_}I felt for youth debarred from its enjoyments by the unnatural vitality of age, and sympathised with the blooming damsel whose parent alone stood between her and her lover.
10095-8{_}2226{_}I thus lived in constant apprehension of being ordered back to the Netherlands, and yearned for the wings of a dove, that I might flee away and be out of mischief.
10095-8{_}2227{_}At last I discovered that my promotion to a higher sphere depended upon my obtaining a testimonial from the reigning Pope.
10095-8{_}2228{_}Let a solemn procession be held in my honour, and intercession be publicly made for me, and I should ascend forthwith.
10095-8{_}2229{_}I have consequently represented my case to many of your predecessors: but, O Alexander, you seventeenth-century Popes are a miserable breed!
10095-8{_}2230{_}No fellow-feeling, no _esprit de corps.
10095-8{_}2231{_}Heu pietas!
10095-8{_}2232{_}heu prisca fides_!
10095-8{_}2233{_}No one was so rude as your ascetic antecessor.
10095-8{_}2234{_}The more of a saint, the less of a gentleman.
10095-8{_}2235{_}Personally offensive, I assure you!
10095-8{_}2236{_}But the others were nearly as bad.
10095-8{_}2237{_}The haughty Paul, the fanatic Gregory, the worldly Urban, the austere Innocent the Tenth, the affable Alexander the Seventh, all concurred in assuring  me that it was deeply to be regretted that I should ever have been emancipated from the restraints of the Stygian realm, to which I should do well to return with all possible celerity; that it would much conduce to the interests of the Church if my name could be forgotten; and that as for doing anything to revive its memory, they would just as soon think of canonising Judas Iscariot."
10095-8{_}2238{_}"And therefore your Holiness has brought these rats upon us, enlisted, I nothing doubt, in the infernal regions?"
10095-8{_}2239{_}"Precisely so: Plutonic, necyomantic, Lemurian rats, kindly lent by the Prince of Darkness for the occasion, and come dripping from Styx to squeak and gibber in the Capitol.
10095-8{_}2240{_}But I note your Holiness's admission that they belong to a region exempt from your jurisdiction, and that, therefore, your measures against them, except as regards their status as belligerents, are for the most part illegitimate and _ultra vires_."
10095-8{_}2241{_}"I would argue that point," replied Alexander the Eighth, "if my lungs were as tough as when I pleaded before the Rota in Pope Urban's time.
10095-8{_}2242{_}For the present I confine myself to formally protesting against your Holiness's unprecedented and parricidal conduct in invading your country at the head of an army of loathsome vermin."
10095-8{_}2243{_}"Unprecedented!"
10095-8{_}2244{_}exclaimed Borgia.
10095-8{_}2245{_}"Am I not the modern Coriolanus?
10095-8{_}2246{_}Did Narses experience blacker ingratitude than I?
10095-8{_}2247{_}Where would the temporal power be but for me?
10095-8{_}2248{_}Who smote the Colonna?
10095-8{_}2249{_}Who squashed the Orsini?
10095-8{_}2250{_}Who gave the Popes to dwell quietly in their own house?
10095-8{_}2251{_}Monsters of unthankfulness!"
10095-8{_}2252{_}"I am sure," said Alexander the Eighth soothingly, "that my predecessors' inability to comply with your Holiness's request must have cost them many inward tears, not the less genuine because entirely invisible and completely inaudible.
10095-8{_}2253{_}A wise Pope will, before all things, consider the spirit of his age.
10095-8{_}2254{_}The force of public opinion, which your Holiness lately appeared to disparage, was, in fact, as operative upon yourself as upon any of your successors.
10095-8{_}2255{_}If you achieved great things in your lifetime, it was because the world was with you.
10095-8{_}2256{_}Did you pursue the same methods now, you would soon discover that you had become an offensive anachronism.
10095-8{_}2257{_}It will not have escaped your Holiness's penetration that what moralists will persist in terming the elevation of the standard of the Church, is the result of the so-called improvement of the world."
10095-8{_}2258{_}"There is a measure of truth in this," admitted Alexander the Sixth, "and the spirit of this age is a very poor spirit.
10095-8{_}2259{_}It was my felicity to be a Pope of the Renaissance.
10095-8{_}2260{_}Blest dispensation!
10095-8{_}2261{_}when men's view of life was large and liberal; when the fair humanities flourished; when the earth yielded up her hoards of chiselled marble and breathing bronze, and new-found agate urns as fresh as day; when painters and sculptors vied with antiquity, and poets and historians followed in their path; when every benign deity was worshipped save Diana and Vesta; when the arts of courtship and cosmetics were expounded by archbishops; when the beauteous Imperia was of more account than the eleven thousand virgins; when obnoxious persons  glided imperceptibly from the world; and no one marvelled if he met the Pope arm in arm with the Devil.
10095-8{_}2262{_}How miserable, in comparison, is the present sapless age, with its prudery and its pedantry, and its periwigs and its painted coaches, and its urban Arcadias and the florid impotence and ostentatious inanity of what it calls its art!
10095-8{_}2263{_}Pope Alexander!
10095-8{_}2264{_}I see in the spirit the sepulchre destined for _you_, and I swear to you that my soul shivers in my ratskins!
10095-8{_}2265{_}Come, now!
10095-8{_}2266{_}I do not expect you to emulate the Popes of my time, but show that your virtues are your own, and your faults those of your epoch.
10095-8{_}2267{_}Pluck up a spirit!
10095-8{_}2268{_}Take bulls by the horns!
10095-8{_}2269{_}Look facts in the face!
10095-8{_}2270{_}Think upon the images of Brutus and Cassius!
10095-8{_}2271{_}Recognise that you cannot get rid of me, and that the only safe course is to rehabilitate me.
10095-8{_}2272{_}I am not a candidate for canonisation just now; but repair past neglect and appease my injured shade in the way you wot of.
10095-8{_}2273{_}If this is done, I pledge my word that every rat shall forthwith evacuate Rome.
10095-8{_}2274{_}Is it a bargain?
10095-8{_}2275{_}I see it is; you are one of the good old sort, though fallen on evil days."
10095-8{_}2276{_}Renaissance or Rats, Alexander the Eighth yielded.
10095-8{_}2277{_}"I promise," he declared.
10095-8{_}2278{_}"Your hand upon it!"
10095-8{_}2279{_}Subduing his repugnance and apprehension by a strong effort, Alexander laid his hand within the spectre's clammy paw.
10095-8{_}2280{_}An icy thrill ran through his veins, and he sank back senseless into his chair.
10095-8{_}2281{_}III   When the Pope recovered consciousness he found himself in bed, with slight symptoms of fever.
10095-8{_}2282{_}His first care was to summon Cardinal Barbadico, and confer with him respecting the surprising adventures which had recently befallen them.
10095-8{_}2283{_}To his amazement, the Cardinal's mind seemed an entire blank on the subject.
10095-8{_}2284{_}He admitted having made his customary report to his Holiness the preceding night, but knew nothing of any supernatural ratcatcher, and nothing of any midnight rendezvous at the Appartamento Borgia.
10095-8{_}2285{_}Investigation seemed to justify his nescience; no vestige of the man of rats or of his shop could be discovered; and the Borgian apartments, opened and carefully searched through, revealed no trace of having been visited for many years.
10095-8{_}2286{_}The Pope's book of exorcisms was in its proper place, his vial of holy water stood unbroken upon his table; and his chamberlains deposed that they had consigned him to Morpheus at the usual hour.
10095-8{_}2287{_}His illusion was at first explained as the effect of a peculiarly vivid dream; but when he declared his intention of actually holding a service and conducting a procession for the weal of his namesake and predecessor, the conviction became universal that the rats had effected a lodgement in his Holiness's upper storeys.
10095-8{_}2288{_}Alexander, notwithstanding, was resolute, and so it came to pass that on the same day two mighty processions encountered within the walls of Rome.
10095-8{_}2289{_}As the assembled clergy, drawn from  all the churches and monasteries in the city, the Pope in his litter in their midst, marched, carrying candles, intoning chants, and, with many a secret shrug and sneer, imploring Heaven for the repose of Alexander the Sixth, they were suddenly brought to bay by another procession precipitated athwart their track, disorderly, repulsive, but more grateful to the sight of the citizens than all the pomps and pageants of the palmiest days of the Papacy.
10095-8{_}2290{_}Black, brown, white, grey; fat and lean; old and young; strident or silent; the whiskered legions tore and galloped along; thronging from every part of the city, they united in single column into an endless host that appeared to stretch from the rising to the setting of the sun.
10095-8{_}2291{_}They seemed making for the Tiber, which they would have speedily choked; but ere they could arrive there a huge rift opened in the earth, down which they madly precipitated themselves.
10095-8{_}2292{_}Their descent, it is affirmed, lasted as many hours as Vulcan occupied in falling from Heaven to Lemnos; but when the last tail was over the brink, the gulf closed as effectually as the gulf in the Forum closed over Marcus Curtius, not leaving the slightest inequality by which any could detect it.
10095-8{_}2293{_}Long ere this consummation had been attained, the Pope, looking forth from his litter, observed a venerable personage clad in ratskins, who appeared desirous of attracting his notice.
10095-8{_}2294{_}Glances of recognition were exchanged, and instantly in place of the ratcatcher stood a tall, swarthy, corpulent, elderly man, with the majestic yet sensual features of Alexander the Sixth, accoutred with the official habiliments and insignia  of a Pope, who rose slowly into the air as though he had been inflated with hydrogen.
10095-8{_}2295{_}"To your prayers!"
10095-8{_}2296{_}cried Alexander the Eighth, and gave the example.
10095-8{_}2297{_}The priesthood resumed its chants, the multitude dropped upon their knees.
10095-8{_}2298{_}Their orisons seemed to speed the ascending figure, which was rising rapidly, when suddenly appeared in air Luxury, Simony, and Cruelty, contending which should receive the Holy Father into her bosom.
10095-8{_}2299{_}[*] Borgia struck at them with his crozier, and seemed to be keeping them at bay, when a cloud wrapped the group from the sight of men.
10095-8{_}2300{_}Thunder roared, lightning glared, the rush of waters blended with the ejaculations of the people and the yet more tempestuous rushing of the rats.
10095-8{_}2301{_}Accompanied as he was, it is not probable that Alexander passed, like Dante's sigh, "beyond the sphere that doth all spheres enfold"; but, as he was never again seen on earth, it is not doubted that he attained at least as far as the moon.
10095-8{_}2302{_}[Footnote:          Per aver riposo   Portato fu fra l'anime beate   Lo spirito di Alessandro glorioso;   Del qual seguiro le sante pedate   Tre sue familiari e care ancelle,   Lussuria, Simonia, e Crudeltate.
10095-8{_}2303{_}[--Machiavelli, _Decennale Primo_.]]
10095-8{_}2304{_}THE REWARDS OF INDUSTRY   In China, under the Tang dynasty, early in the seventh century of the Christian era, lived a learned and virtuous, but poor mandarin who had three sons, Fu-su, Tu-sin, and Wang-li.
10095-8{_}2305{_}Fu-su and Tu-sin were young men of active minds, always labouring to find out something new and useful.
10095-8{_}2306{_}Wang-li was clever too, but only in games of skill, in which he attained great proficiency.
10095-8{_}2307{_}Fu-su and Tu-sin continually talked to each other of the wonderful inventions they would make when they arrived at man's estate, and of the wealth and renown they promised themselves thereby.
10095-8{_}2308{_}Their conversation seldom reached the ears of Wang-li, for he rarely lifted his eyes from the chess-board on which he solved his problems.
10095-8{_}2309{_}But their father was more attentive, and one day he said:  "I fear, my sons, that among your multifarious pursuits and studies you must have omitted to include that of the laws of your country, or you would have learned that fortune is not to be acquired by the means which you have proposed to yourselves."
10095-8{_}2310{_}"How so, father?"
10095-8{_}2311{_}asked they.
10095-8{_}2312{_}"It hath been justly deemed by our ancestors," said the old man, "that the reverence due to the  great men who are worshipped in our temples, by reason of our indebtedness to them for the arts of life, could not but become impaired if their posterity were suffered to eclipse their fame by new discoveries, or presumptuously amend what might appear imperfect in their productions.
10095-8{_}2313{_}It is therefore, by an edict of the Emperor Suen, forbidden to invent anything; and by a statute of the Emperor Wu-chi it is further provided that nothing hitherto invented shall be improved.
10095-8{_}2314{_}My predecessor in the small office I hold was deprived of it for saying that in his judgment money ought to be made round instead of square, and I have myself run risk of my life for seeking to combine a small file with a pair of tweezers."
10095-8{_}2315{_}"If this is the case," said the young men, "our fatherland is not the place for us."
10095-8{_}2316{_}And they embraced their father, and departed.
10095-8{_}2317{_}Of their brother Wang-li they took no farewell, inasmuch as he was absorbed in a chess problem.
10095-8{_}2318{_}Before separating, they agreed to meet on the same spot after thirty years, with the treasure which they doubted not to have acquired by the exercise of their inventive faculties in foreign lands.
10095-8{_}2319{_}They further covenanted that if either had missed his reward the other should share his possessions with him.
10095-8{_}2320{_}Fu-su repaired to the artists who cut out characters in blocks of hard wood, to the end that books may be printed from the same.
10095-8{_}2321{_}When he had fathomed their mystery he betook himself to a brass-founder, and learned how to cast in metal.
10095-8{_}2322{_}He then sought a learned man who had travelled much, and made himself acquainted with the Greek, Persian, and Arabic languages.
10095-8{_}2323{_}Then he  cast a number of Greek characters in type, and putting them into a bag and providing himself with some wooden letter-tablets of his own carving, he departed to seek his fortune.
10095-8{_}2324{_}After innumerable hardships and perils he arrived in the land of Persia, and inquired for the great king.
10095-8{_}2325{_}"The great king is dead," they told him, "and his head is entirely separated from his body.
10095-8{_}2326{_}There is now no king in Persia, great or small."
10095-8{_}2327{_}"Where shall I find another great king?"
10095-8{_}2328{_}demanded he.
10095-8{_}2329{_}"In the city of Alexandria," replied they, "where the Commander of the Faithful is busy introducing the religion of the Prophet."
10095-8{_}2330{_}Fu-su passed to Alexandria, carrying his types and tablets.
10095-8{_}2331{_}As he entered the gates he remarked an enormous cloud of smoke, which seemed to darken the whole city.
10095-8{_}2332{_}Before he could inquire the reason, the guard arrested him as a stranger, and conducted him to the presence of the Caliph Omar.
10095-8{_}2333{_}"Know, O Caliph," said Fu-su, "that my countrymen are at once the wisest of mankind and the stupidest.
10095-8{_}2334{_}They have invented an art for the preservation of letters and the diffusion of knowledge, which the sages of Greece and India never knew, but they have not learned to take, and they refuse to be taught how to take, the one little step further necessary to render it generally profitable to mankind."
10095-8{_}2335{_}And producing his tablets and types, he explained to the Caliph the entire mystery of the art of printing.
10095-8{_}2336{_}"Thou seemest to be ignorant," said Omar, "that we have but yesterday condemned and  excommunicated all books, and banished the same from the face of the earth, seeing that they contain either that which is contrary to the Koran, in which case they are impious, or that which is agreeable to the Koran, in which case they are superfluous.
10095-8{_}2337{_}Thou art further unaware, as it would seem, that the smoke which shrouds the city proceeds from the library of the unbelievers, consumed by our orders.
10095-8{_}2338{_}It will be meet to burn thee along with it."
10095-8{_}2339{_}"O Commander of the Faithful," said an officer, "of a surety the last scroll of the accursed ceased to flame even as this infidel entered the city."
10095-8{_}2340{_}"If it be so," said Omar, "we will not burn him, seeing that we have taken away from him the occasion to sin.
10095-8{_}2341{_}Yet shall he swallow these little brass amulets of his, at the rate of one a day, and then be banished from the country."
10095-8{_}2342{_}The sentence was executed, and Fu-su was happy that the Court physician condescended to accept his little property in exchange for emetics.
10095-8{_}2343{_}He begged his way slowly and painfully back to China, and arrived at the covenanted spot at the expiration of the thirtieth year.
10095-8{_}2344{_}His father's modest dwelling had disappeared, and in its place stood a magnificent mansion, around which stretched a park with pavilions, canals, willow-trees, golden pheasants, and little bridges.
10095-8{_}2345{_}"Tu-sin has surely made his fortune," thought he, "and he will not refuse to share it with me agreeably to our covenant."
10095-8{_}2346{_}As he thus reflected he heard a voice at his elbow, and turning round perceived that one in a more wretched plight than himself was asking alms of him.
10095-8{_}2347{_}It was Tu-sin.
10095-8{_}2348{_}The brothers embraced with many tears, and after Tu-sin had learned Fu-su's history, he proceeded to recount his own.
10095-8{_}2349{_}"I repaired," said he, "to those who know the secret of the grains termed fire-dust, which Suen has not been able to prevent us from inventing, but of which Wu-chi has taken care that we shall make no use, save only for fireworks.
10095-8{_}2350{_}Having learned their mystery I deposited a certain portion of this fire-dust in hollow tubes which I had constructed of iron and brass, and upon it I further laid leaden balls of a size corresponding to the hollow of the tubes.
10095-8{_}2351{_}I then found that by applying a light to the fire-dust at one end of the tube I could send the ball out at the other with such force that it penetrated the cuirasses of three warriors at once.
10095-8{_}2352{_}I filled a barrel with the dust, and concealing it and the tubes under carpets which I laid upon the backs of oxen, I set out to the city of Constantinople.
10095-8{_}2353{_}I will not at present relate my adventures on the journey.
10095-8{_}2354{_}Suffice it that I arrived at last half dead from fatigue and hardship, and destitute of everything except my merchandise.
10095-8{_}2355{_}By bribing an officer with my carpets I was admitted to have speech with the Emperor.
10095-8{_}2356{_}I found him busily studying a problem in chess.
10095-8{_}2357{_}"I told him that I had discovered a secret which would make him the master of the world, and in particular would help him to drive away the Saracens, who threatened his empire with destruction.
10095-8{_}2358{_}"'Thou must perceive,' he said, 'that I cannot possibly attend to thee until I have solved this problem.
10095-8{_}2359{_}Yet, lest any should say that the Emperor neglects his duties, absorbed in idle amusement, I will refer thy invention to the chief armourers of my capital.
10095-8{_}2360{_}And he gave me a letter to the armourers, and returned to his problem.
10095-8{_}2361{_}And as I quitted the palace bearing the missive, I came upon a great procession.
10095-8{_}2362{_}Horsemen and running footmen, musicians, heralds, and banner-bearers surrounded a Chinaman who sat in the attitude of Fo under a golden umbrella upon a richly caparisoned elephant, his pigtail plaited with yellow roses.
10095-8{_}2363{_}And the musicians blew and clashed, and the standard-bearers waved their ensigns, and the heralds proclaimed, 'Thus shall it be done to the man whom the Emperor delights to honour.'
10095-8{_}2364{_}And unless I was very greatly mistaken, the face of the Chinaman was the face of our brother Wang-li.
10095-8{_}2365{_}"At another time I would have striven to find what this might mean, but my impatience was great, as also my need and hunger.
10095-8{_}2366{_}I sought the chief armourers, and with great trouble brought them all together to give me audience, I produced my tube and fire-dust, and sent my balls with ease through the best armour they could set before me.  "'
10095-8{_}2367{_}Who will want breast-plates now?'
10095-8{_}2368{_}cried the chief breast-plate maker.
10095-8{_}2369{_}"'Or helmets?'
10095-8{_}2370{_}exclaimed one who made armour for the head.
10095-8{_}2371{_}"'I would not have taken fifty bezants for that shield, and what good is it now?'
10095-8{_}2372{_}said the head of the shield trade.
10095-8{_}2373{_}"'My swords will be of less account,' said a swordsmith.
10095-8{_}2374{_}"'My arrows of none,' lamented an arrow-maker.
10095-8{_}2375{_}"''Tis villainy,' cried one.
10095-8{_}2376{_}"''Tis magic,' shouted another.
10095-8{_}2377{_}"''Tis illusion, as I'm an honest tradesman,' roared a third, and put his integrity to the proof by thrusting a hot iron bar into my barrel.
10095-8{_}2378{_}All present rose up in company with the roof of the building, and all perished, except myself, who escaped with the loss of my hair and skin.
10095-8{_}2379{_}A fire broke out on the spot, and consumed one-third of the city of Constantinople.
10095-8{_}2380{_}"I was lying on a prison-bed some time afterwards, partly recovered of my hurts, dolefully listening to a dispute between two of my guards as to whether I ought to be burned or buried alive, when the Imperial order for my disposal came down.
10095-8{_}2381{_}The gaolers received it with humility, and read 'Kick him out of the city.'
10095-8{_}2382{_}Marvelling at the mildness of the punishment, they nevertheless executed it with so much zeal that I flew into the middle of the Bosphorus, where I was picked up by a fishing vessel, and landed on the Asiatic coast, whence I have begged my way home.
10095-8{_}2383{_}I now propose that we appeal to the pity of the owner of this splendid mansion, who may compassionate us on hearing that we were reared in the Cottage which has been pulled down to make room for his palace."
10095-8{_}2384{_}They entered the gates, walked timidly up to the house, and prepared to fall at the feet of the master, but did not, for ere they could do so they recognised their brother Wang-li.
10095-8{_}2385{_}It took Wang-li some time to recognise them, but when at length he knew them he hastened to  provide for their every want.
10095-8{_}2386{_}When they had well eaten and drunk, and had been clad in robes of honour, they imparted their histories, and asked for his.
10095-8{_}2387{_}"My brothers," said Wang-li, "the noble game of chess, which was happily invented long before the time of the Emperor Suen, was followed by me solely for its pleasure, and I dreamed not of acquiring wealth by its pursuit until I casually heard one day that it was entirely unknown to the people of the West.
10095-8{_}2388{_}Even then I thought not of gaining money, but conceived so deep a compassion for those forlorn barbarians that I felt I could know no rest until I should have enlightened them.
10095-8{_}2389{_}I accordingly proceeded to the city of Constantinople, and was received as a messenger from Heaven.
10095-8{_}2390{_}To such effect did I labour that ere long the Emperor and his officers of state thought of nothing else but playing chess all day and night, and the empire fell into entire confusion, and the Saracens mightily prevailed.
10095-8{_}2391{_}In consideration of these services the Emperor was pleased to bestow those distinguished honours upon me which thou didst witness at his palace gate, dear brother.
10095-8{_}2392{_}"After, however, the fire which was occasioned through thy instrumentality, though in no respect by thy fault, the people murmured, and taxed the Emperor with seeking to destroy his capital in league with a foreign sorcerer, meaning thee.
10095-8{_}2393{_}Ere long the chief officers conspired and entered the Emperor's apartment, purposing to dethrone him, but he declared that he would in nowise abdicate until he had finished the game of chess he was then playing with me.
10095-8{_}2394{_}They looked on, grew  interested, began to dispute with one another respecting the moves, and while they wrangled loyal officers entered and made them all captive.
10095-8{_}2395{_}This greatly augmented my credit with the Emperor, which was even increased when shortly afterwards I played with the Saracen admiral blockading the Hellespont, and won of him forty corn-ships, which turned the dearth of the city into plenty.
10095-8{_}2396{_}"The Emperor bade me choose any favour I would, but I said his liberality had left me nothing to ask for except the life of a poor countryman of mine who I had heard was in prison for burning the city.
10095-8{_}2397{_}The Emperor bade me write his sentence with my own hand.
10095-8{_}2398{_}Had I known that it was thou, Tu-sin, believe me I had shown more consideration for thy person.
10095-8{_}2399{_}At length I departed for my native land, loaded with wealth, and travelling most comfortably by relays of swift dromedaries.
10095-8{_}2400{_}I returned hither, bought our father's cottage, and on its site erected this palace, where I dwell meditating on the problems of chessplayers and the precepts of the sages, and persuaded that a little thing which the world is willing to receive is better than a great thing which it hath not yet learned to value aright.
10095-8{_}2401{_}For the world is a big child, and chooses amusement before instruction."
10095-8{_}2402{_}"Call you chess an amusement?"
10095-8{_}2403{_}asked his brothers.
10095-8{_}2404{_}MADAM LUCIFER   Lucifer sat playing chess with Man for his soul.
10095-8{_}2405{_}The game was evidently going ill for Man.
10095-8{_}2406{_}He had but pawns left, few and straggling.
10095-8{_}2407{_}Lucifer had rooks, knights, and, of course, bishops.
10095-8{_}2408{_}It was but natural under such circumstances that Man should be in no great hurry to move.
10095-8{_}2409{_}Lucifer grew impatient.
10095-8{_}2410{_}"It is a pity," said he at last, "that we did not fix some period within which the player must move, or resign."
10095-8{_}2411{_}"Oh, Lucifer," returned the young man, in heart-rending accents, "it is not the impending loss of my soul that thus unmans me, but the loss of my betrothed.
10095-8{_}2412{_}When I think of the grief of the Lady Adeliza, that paragon of terrestrial loveliness!"
10095-8{_}2413{_}Tears choked his utterance; Lucifer was touched.
10095-8{_}2414{_}"Is the Lady Adeliza's loveliness in sooth so transcendent?"
10095-8{_}2415{_}he inquired.
10095-8{_}2416{_}"She is a rose, a lily, a diamond, a morning star!"
10095-8{_}2417{_}"If that is the case," rejoined Lucifer, "thou mayest reassure thyself.
10095-8{_}2418{_}The Lady Adeliza shall not want for consolation.
10095-8{_}2419{_}I will assume thy shape and woo her in thy stead."
10095-8{_}2420{_}The young man hardly seemed to receive all the comfort from this promise which Lucifer no doubt designed.
10095-8{_}2421{_}He made a desperate move.
10095-8{_}2422{_}In an instant the Devil checkmated him, and he disappeared.
10095-8{_}2423{_}*       *       *       *       *  "Upon my word, if I had known what a business this was going to be, I don't think I should have gone in for it," soliloquised the Devil, as, wearing his captive's semblance and installed in his apartments, he surveyed the effects to which he now had to administer.
10095-8{_}2424{_}They included coats, shirts, collars, neckties, foils, cigars, and the like _ad libitum_; and very little else except three challenges, ten writs, and seventy-four unpaid bills, elegantly disposed around the looking-glass.
10095-8{_}2425{_}To the poor youth's praise be it said, there were no billets-doux, except from the Lady Adeliza herself.
10095-8{_}2426{_}Noting the address of these carefully, the Devil sallied forth, and nothing but his ignorance of the topography of the hotel, which made him take the back stairs, saved him from the clutches of two bailiffs lurking on the principal staircase.
10095-8{_}2427{_}Leaping into a cab, he thus escaped a perfumer and a bootmaker, and shortly found himself at the Lady Adeliza's feet.
10095-8{_}2428{_}The truth had not been half told him.
10095-8{_}2429{_}Such beauty, such wit, such correctness of principle!
10095-8{_}2430{_}Lucifer went forth from her presence a love-sick fiend.
10095-8{_}2431{_}Not Merlin's mother had produced half the impression upon him; and Adeliza on her part had never found her lover one-hundredth part so interesting as he seemed that morning.
10095-8{_}2432{_}Lucifer proceeded at once to the City, where,  assuming his proper shape for the occasion, he negotiated a loan without the smallest difficulty.
10095-8{_}2433{_}All debts were promptly discharged, and Adeliza was astonished at the splendour and variety of the presents she was constantly receiving.
10095-8{_}2434{_}Lucifer had all but brought her to name the day, when he was informed that a gentleman of clerical appearance desired to wait upon him.
10095-8{_}2435{_}"Wants money for a new church or mission, I suppose," said he.
10095-8{_}2436{_}"Show him up."
10095-8{_}2437{_}But when the visitor was ushered in, Lucifer found with discomposure that he was no earthly clergyman, but a celestial saint; a saint, too, with whom Lucifer had never been able to get on.
10095-8{_}2438{_}He had served in the army while on earth, and his address was curt, precise, and peremptory.
10095-8{_}2439{_}"I have called," he said, "to notify to you my appointment as Inspector of Devils."
10095-8{_}2440{_}"What!"
10095-8{_}2441{_}exclaimed Lucifer, in consternation.
10095-8{_}2442{_}"To the post of my old friend Michael!"
10095-8{_}2443{_}"Too old," said the Saint laconically.
10095-8{_}2444{_}"Millions of years older than the world.
10095-8{_}2445{_}About your age, I think?"
10095-8{_}2446{_}Lucifer winced, remembering the particular business he was then about.
10095-8{_}2447{_}The Saint continued:  "I am a new broom, and am expected to sweep clean.
10095-8{_}2448{_}I warn you that I mean to be strict, and there is one little matter which I must set right immediately.
10095-8{_}2449{_}You are going to marry that poor young fellow's betrothed, are you?
10095-8{_}2450{_}Now you know you cannot take his wife, unless you give him yours."
10095-8{_}2451{_}"Oh, my dear friend," exclaimed Lucifer, "what an inexpressibly blissful prospect you do open unto me!"
10095-8{_}2452{_}"I don't know that," said the Saint.
10095-8{_}2453{_}"I must remind you that the dominion of the infernal regions is unalterably attached to the person of the present Queen thereof.
10095-8{_}2454{_}If you part with her you immediately lose all your authority and possessions.
10095-8{_}2455{_}I don't care a brass button which you do, but you must understand that you cannot eat your cake and have it too.
10095-8{_}2456{_}Good morning!"
10095-8{_}2457{_}Who shall describe the conflict in Lucifer's bosom?
10095-8{_}2458{_}If any stronger passion existed therein at that moment than attachment to Adeliza, it was aversion to his consort, and the two combined were well-nigh irresistible.
10095-8{_}2459{_}But to disenthrone himself, to descend to the condition of a poor devil!
10095-8{_}2460{_}Feeling himself incapable of coming to a decision, he sent for Belial, unfolded the matter, and requested his advice.
10095-8{_}2461{_}"What a shame that our new inspector will not let you marry Adeliza!"
10095-8{_}2462{_}lamented his counsellor.
10095-8{_}2463{_}"If you did, my private opinion is that forty-eight hours afterwards you would care just as much for her as you do now for Madam Lucifer, neither more nor less.
10095-8{_}2464{_}Are your intentions really honourable?"
10095-8{_}2465{_}"Yes," replied Lucifer, "it is to be a Lucifer match."
10095-8{_}2466{_}"The more fool you," rejoined Belial.
10095-8{_}2467{_}"If you tempted her to commit a sin, she would be yours without any conditions at all."
10095-8{_}2468{_}"Oh, Belial," said Lucifer, "I cannot bring myself to be a tempter of so much innocence and loveliness."
10095-8{_}2469{_}And he meant what he said.
10095-8{_}2470{_}"Well then, let me try," proposed Belial.
10095-8{_}2471{_}"You?"
10095-8{_}2472{_}replied Lucifer contemptuously; "do you imagine that Adeliza would look at _you_?"
10095-8{_}2473{_}"Why not?"
10095-8{_}2474{_}asked Belial, surveying himself complacently in the glass.
10095-8{_}2475{_}He was humpbacked, squinting, and lame, and his horns stood up under his wig.
10095-8{_}2476{_}The discussion ended in a wager after which there was no retreat for Lucifer.
10095-8{_}2477{_}The infernal Iachimo was introduced to Adeliza as a distinguished foreigner, and was soon prosecuting his suit with all the success which Lucifer had predicted.
10095-8{_}2478{_}One thing protected while it baffled him--the entire inability of Adeliza to understand what he meant.
10095-8{_}2479{_}At length he was constrained to make the matter clear by producing an enormous treasure, which he offered Adeliza in exchange for the abandonment of her lover.
10095-8{_}2480{_}The tempest of indignation which ensued would have swept away any ordinary demon, but Belial listened unmoved.
10095-8{_}2481{_}When Adeliza had exhausted herself he smilingly rallied her upon her affection for an unworthy lover, of whose infidelity he undertook to give her proof.
10095-8{_}2482{_}Frantic with jealousy, Adeliza consented, and in a trice found herself in the infernal regions.
10095-8{_}2483{_}*       *       *       *       *  Adeliza's arrival in Pandemonium, as Belial had planned, occurred immediately after the receipt of a message from Lucifer, in whose bosom love had finally gained the victory, and who had telegraphed his abdication and resignation of Madam Lucifer to Adeliza's betrothed.
10095-8{_}2484{_}The poor young man had just been hauled up from the lower depths, and was beset by legions of demons obsequiously pressing all manner of treasures upon his acceptance.
10095-8{_}2485{_}He stared, helpless and  bewildered, unable to realise his position in the smallest degree.

10095-8{_}2487{_}"Stay where you are," whispered Belial to Adeliza; "stir not; you shall put his constancy to the proof within five minutes."
10095-8{_}2488{_}Not all the hustling, mowing, and gibbering of the fiends would under ordinary circumstances have kept Adeliza from her lover's side: but what is all hell to jealousy?
10095-8{_}2489{_}In even less time than he had promised Belial returned, accompanied by Madam Lucifer.
10095-8{_}2490{_}This lady's black robe, dripping with blood, contrasted agreeably with her complexion of sulphurous yellow; the absence of hair was compensated by the exceptional length of her nails; she was a thousand million years old, and, but for her remarkable muscular vigour, looked every one of them.
10095-8{_}2491{_}The rage into which Belial's communication had thrown her was something indescribable; but, as her eye fell on the handsome youth, a different order of thoughts seemed to take possession of her mind.
10095-8{_}2492{_}"Let the monster go!"
10095-8{_}2493{_}she exclaimed; "who cares?

10095-8{_}2495{_}"If you don't, back you go," interjected Belial.
10095-8{_}2496{_}What might have been the young man's decision if Madam Lucifer had borne more resemblance to Madam Vulcan, it would be wholly impertinent to inquire, for the question never arose.
10095-8{_}2497{_}"Take me away!"
10095-8{_}2498{_}he screamed, "take me away, anywhere I anywhere out of her reach!
10095-8{_}2499{_}Oh, Adeliza!"
10095-8{_}2500{_}With a bound Adeliza stood by his side.
10095-8{_}2501{_}She was darting a triumphant glance at the discomfited Queen of Hell, when suddenly her expression changed, and she screamed loudly.
10095-8{_}2502{_}Two adorers stood before her, alike in every lineament and every detail of costume, utterly indistinguishable, even by the eye of Love.
10095-8{_}2503{_}Lucifer, in fact, hastening to throw himself at Adeliza's feet and pray her to defer his bliss no longer, had been thunderstruck by the tidings of her elopement with Belial.
10095-8{_}2504{_}Fearing to lose his wife and his dominions along with his sweetheart, he had sped to the nether regions with such expedition that he had had no time to change his costume.
10095-8{_}2505{_}Hence the equivocation which confounded Adeliza, but at the same time preserved her from being torn to pieces by the no less mystified Madam Lucifer.
